Government forces were poorly equipped and unprepared for the war.<sup id="cite_ref-ICTY:_NaletiliÄ_and_MartinoviÄ_verdict&nbsp;â_A._Historical_background_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ICTY:_NaletiliÄ_and_MartinoviÄ_verdict_â_A._Historical_background-87">[85]</a></sup> International recognition of Bosnia and Herzegovina increased diplomatic pressure for the <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_People%27s_Army" title="Yugoslav People's Army">Yugoslav People's Army</a> (JNA) to withdraw from the republic's territory, which they officially did in June 1992. The Bosnian Serb members of the JNA simply changed insignia, formed the <a href="/wiki/Army_of_Republika_Srpska" title="Army of Republika Srpska">Army of Republika Srpska</a> (VRS), and continued fighting. Armed and equipped from JNA stockpiles in Bosnia, supported by volunteers and various paramilitary forces from Serbia, and receiving extensive humanitarian, logistical and financial support from the <a href="/wiki/Serbia_and_Montenegro" title="Serbia and Montenegro">Federal Republic of Yugoslavia</a>, Republika Srpska's offensives in 1992 managed to place much of the country under its control.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMalcolm2002_19-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMalcolm2002-19">[17]</a></sup> The Bosnian Serb advance was accompanied by the <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_cleansing" title="Ethnic cleansing">ethnic cleansing</a> of Bosniaks and Bosnian Croats from VRS-controlled areas. Dozens of concentration camps were established in which inmates were subjected to violence and abuse, including rape.<sup id="cite_ref-ICTY:_Kunarac,_KovaÄ_and_VukoviÄ_judgement&nbsp;â_FoÄa_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ICTY:_Kunarac,_KovaÄ_and_VukoviÄ_judgement_â_FoÄa-88">[86]</a></sup> The ethnic cleansing culminated in the <a href="/wiki/Srebrenica_massacre" title="Srebrenica massacre">Srebrenica massacre</a> of more than 8,000 Bosniak men and boys in July 1995, which was ruled to have been a <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">genocide</a> by the ICTY.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[87]</a></sup> Bosniak and Bosnian Croat forces also committed war crimes against civilians from different ethnic groups, though on a smaller scale.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[88]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[89]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-haverford_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-haverford-92">[90]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-un_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-un-93">[91]</a></sup> Most of the Bosniak and Croat atrocities were committed during the <a href="/wiki/Bosniak-Croat_war" class="mw-redirect" title="Bosniak-Croat war">Bosniak-Croat war</a>, a sub-conflict of the Bosnian War that pitted the <a href="/wiki/Army_of_the_Federation_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Army of the Federation of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Army of the Federation of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> (ARBiH) against the HVO. The Bosniak-Croat conflict ended in March 1994, with the signing of the <a href="/wiki/Washington_Agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="Washington Agreement">Washington Agreement</a>, leading to the creation of a joint Bosniak-Croat <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Federation of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Federation of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>, which amalgamated HVO-held territory with that held by the ARBiH.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bk-map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Bk-map.png/220px-Bk-map.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="236" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/7a/Bk-map.png 1.5x" data-file-width="326" data-file-height="350"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bk-map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Bosnia and Herzegovina after the <a href="/wiki/Dayton_Agreement" title="Dayton Agreement">Dayton Agreement</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_history">Recent history</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/2014_riots_in_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" class="mw-redirect" title="2014 riots in Bosnia and Herzegovina">2014 riots in Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bosnian_social_protests_Tuzla.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Bosnian_social_protests_Tuzla.jpg/200px-Bosnian_social_protests_Tuzla.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="113" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Bosnian_social_protests_Tuzla.jpg/300px-Bosnian_social_protests_Tuzla.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Bosnian_social_protests_Tuzla.jpg/400px-Bosnian_social_protests_Tuzla.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="541"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bosnian_social_protests_Tuzla.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Tuzla government building burning after anti-government clashes on 7 February 2014
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>On 4 February 2014, the protests against the government of the <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Federation of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Federation of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>, one of the country's two entities, dubbed the <b>Bosnian Spring</b>, the name being taken from the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Spring" title="Arab Spring">Arab Spring</a>, began in the northern town of <a href="/wiki/Tuzla" title="Tuzla">Tuzla</a>. Workers from several factories that had been privatised and had gone bankrupt united to demand action over jobs, and unpaid salaries and pensions.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[92]</a></sup> Soon protests spread to the rest of the Federation, with violent clashes reported in close to 20 towns, the biggest of which were <a href="/wiki/Sarajevo" title="Sarajevo">Sarajevo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zenica" title="Zenica">Zenica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mostar" title="Mostar">Mostar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biha%C4%87" title="BihaÄ">BihaÄ</a>, <a href="/wiki/Br%C4%8Dko" title="BrÄko">BrÄko</a> and Tuzla.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[93]</a></sup> The Bosnian news media reported hundreds of people had been injured during the protests, including dozens of police officers, with bursts of violence in Sarajevo, in the northern city of Tuzla, in Mostar in the south, and in Zenica in central Bosnia. The same level of unrest or activism did not occur in the <a href="/wiki/Republika_Srpska" title="Republika Srpska">Republika Srpska</a>, but hundreds of people also gathered in support of protests in the town of <a href="/wiki/Banja_Luka" title="Banja Luka">Banja Luka</a> against its separate government.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[94]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[95]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[96]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The protests marked the largest outbreak of public anger over high unemployment and two decades of political inertia in the country since the end of the Bosnian War in 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[97]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Geography of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Geography of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_mountains_in_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="List of mountains in Bosnia and Herzegovina">List of mountains in Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_lakes_in_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" class="mw-redirect" title="List of lakes in Bosnia and Herzegovina">List of lakes in Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_rivers_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="List of rivers of Bosnia and Herzegovina">List of rivers of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Bosnia is in the western <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a>, bordering <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a> (932&nbsp;km or 579&nbsp;mi) to the north and west, <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> (302&nbsp;km or 188&nbsp;mi) to the east, and <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a> (225&nbsp;km or 140&nbsp;mi) to the southeast. It has a coastline about 20 kilometres (12 miles) long surrounding the city of <a href="/wiki/Neum" title="Neum">Neum</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-coastline_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coastline-100">[98]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[99]</a></sup> It lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/42nd_parallel_north" title="42nd parallel north">42Â°</a> and <a href="/wiki/46th_parallel_north" title="46th parallel north">46Â° N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/15th_meridian_east" title="15th meridian east">15Â°</a> and <a href="/wiki/20th_meridian_east" title="20th meridian east">20Â° E</a>. </p>
      <p>The country's name comes from the two alleged regions <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_(region)" title="Bosnia (region)">Bosnia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Herzegovina" title="Herzegovina">Herzegovina</a> whose border was never defined. Historically, Bosnia's official name never included any of its many regions until the Austria-Hungarian occupation. </p> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_topographic_map.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_topographic_map.svg/200px-Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_topographic_map.svg.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="183" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_topographic_map.svg/300px-Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_topographic_map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_topographic_map.svg/400px-Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_topographic_map.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="549"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption text-align-center">
           <a href="/wiki/Topographic_map" title="Topographic map">Topographic map</a> of Bosnia and Herzegovina
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:River_Bosna,_Sarajevo_(4).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/River_Bosna%2C_Sarajevo_%284%29.JPG/200px-River_Bosna%2C_Sarajevo_%284%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/River_Bosna%2C_Sarajevo_%284%29.JPG/300px-River_Bosna%2C_Sarajevo_%284%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/River_Bosna%2C_Sarajevo_%284%29.JPG/400px-River_Bosna%2C_Sarajevo_%284%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption text-align-center">
           <a href="/wiki/Bosna_(river)" title="Bosna (river)">Bosna</a> river, <a href="/wiki/Ilid%C5%BEa" title="IlidÅ¾a">IlidÅ¾a</a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The country is mostly mountainous, encompassing the central <a href="/wiki/Dinaric_Alps" title="Dinaric Alps">Dinaric Alps</a>. The northeastern parts reach into the <a href="/wiki/Pannonian_Plain" class="mw-redirect" title="Pannonian Plain">Pannonian Plain</a>, while in the south it borders the <a href="/wiki/Adriatic_Sea" title="Adriatic Sea">Adriatic</a>. The Dinaric Alps generally run in a southeastânorthwest direction, and get higher towards the south. The highest point of the country is the peak of <a href="/wiki/Magli%C4%87_(mountain)" title="MagliÄ (mountain)">MagliÄ</a> at 2,386 metres (7,828.1 feet), on the Montenegrin border. Major mountains include <a href="/wiki/Kozara" title="Kozara">Kozara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grme%C4%8D" title="GrmeÄ">GrmeÄ</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vla%C5%A1i%C4%87_(Bosnian_mountain)" title="VlaÅ¡iÄ (Bosnian mountain)">VlaÅ¡iÄ</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C4%8Cvrsnica_Mountain" class="mw-redirect" title="Ävrsnica Mountain">Ävrsnica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prenj" title="Prenj">Prenj</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romanija" title="Romanija">Romanija</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jahorina" title="Jahorina">Jahorina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bjela%C5%A1nica_Mountain" class="mw-redirect" title="BjelaÅ¡nica Mountain">BjelaÅ¡nica</a> and <a href="/wiki/Treskavica" title="Treskavica">Treskavica</a>. The geological composition of the Dinaric chain of mountains in Bosnia consists primarily of <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Mesozoic" title="Mesozoic">Mesozoic</a> limestone), with deposits of <a href="/wiki/Iron" title="Iron">iron</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coal" title="Coal">coal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zinc" title="Zinc">zinc</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manganese" title="Manganese">manganese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bauxite" title="Bauxite">bauxite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lead" title="Lead">lead</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Salt" title="Salt">salt</a> present in some areas, especially in central and northern Bosnia.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[100]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Overall, nearly 50% of Bosnia and Herzegovina is forested. Most forest areas are in the centre, east and west parts of Bosnia. Herzegovina has drier Mediterranean climate, with dominant <a href="/wiki/Karst" title="Karst">karst</a> topography. Northern Bosnia (<a href="/wiki/Posavina" title="Posavina">Posavina</a>) contains very fertile agricultural land along the River Sava and the corresponding area is heavily farmed. This farmland is a part of the Pannonian Plain stretching into neighboring Croatia and Serbia. The country has only 20 kilometres (12 miles) of coastline,<sup id="cite_ref-coastline_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coastline-100">[98]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Neum_coastline_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Neum_coastline-103">[101]</a></sup> around the town of <a href="/wiki/Neum" title="Neum">Neum</a> in the Herzegovina-Neretva Canton. Although the city is surrounded by Croatian peninsulas, by international law, Bosnia and Herzegovina has a <a href="/wiki/Right_of_passage" title="Right of passage">right of passage</a> to the outer sea. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Sarajevo" title="Sarajevo">Sarajevo</a> is the capital<sup id="cite_ref-Constitution_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-1">[1]</a></sup> and largest city.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECIA2019_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECIA2019-4">[4]</a></sup> Other major cities are <a href="/wiki/Banja_Luka" title="Banja Luka">Banja Luka</a> and <a href="/wiki/Biha%C4%87" title="BihaÄ">BihaÄ</a> in the northwest region known as <a href="/wiki/Bosanska_Krajina" title="Bosanska Krajina">Bosanska Krajina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bijeljina" title="Bijeljina">Bijeljina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tuzla" title="Tuzla">Tuzla</a> in the northeast, <a href="/wiki/Zenica" title="Zenica">Zenica</a> in the central part of Bosnia and <a href="/wiki/Mostar" title="Mostar">Mostar</a>, the largest city in <a href="/wiki/Herzegovina" title="Herzegovina">Herzegovina</a>. </p>
      <p>There are seven major rivers in Bosnia and Herzegovina:<sup id="cite_ref-fao_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fao-104">[102]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Trnova%C4%8Dko_jezero,_Magli%C4%87.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Trnova%C4%8Dko_jezero%2C_Magli%C4%87.jpg/200px-Trnova%C4%8Dko_jezero%2C_Magli%C4%87.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Trnova%C4%8Dko_jezero%2C_Magli%C4%87.jpg/300px-Trnova%C4%8Dko_jezero%2C_Magli%C4%87.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Trnova%C4%8Dko_jezero%2C_Magli%C4%87.jpg/400px-Trnova%C4%8Dko_jezero%2C_Magli%C4%87.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1500"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Trnova%C4%8Dko_jezero,_Magli%C4%87.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>MagliÄ Mts. (from TrnovaÄko lake in Montenegro)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r852221607">.mw-parser-output .flowlist ul{overflow-x:hidden;margin-left:0;padding-left:1.6em}.mw-parser-output .flowlist ol{overflow-x:hidden;margin-left:0;padding-left:3.2em}.mw-parser-output .flowlist dl{overflow-x:hidden}</style>
      <div class="flowlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>The <a href="/wiki/Sava" title="Sava">Sava</a> is the largest river of the country, and forms its northern <a href="/wiki/Natural_border" title="Natural border">natural border</a> with Croatia. It drains 76%<sup id="cite_ref-fao_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fao-104">[102]</a></sup> of the country's territory into the Danube and then the Black Sea. Bosnia and Herzegovina is a member of the <a href="/wiki/International_Commission_for_the_Protection_of_the_Danube_River" title="International Commission for the Protection of the Danube River">International Commission for the Protection of the Danube River</a> (ICPDR).</li> 
        <li>The <a href="/wiki/Una_(Sava)" title="Una (Sava)">Una</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sana_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Sana River">Sana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vrbas_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Vrbas River">Vrbas</a> are right tributaries of Sava river. They are in the northwestern region of Bosanska Krajina.</li> 
        <li>The <a href="/wiki/Bosna_(river)" title="Bosna (river)">Bosna</a> river gave its name to the country, and is the longest river fully contained within it. It stretches through central Bosnia, from its source near <a href="/wiki/Sarajevo" title="Sarajevo">Sarajevo</a> to Sava in the north.</li> 
        <li>The <a href="/wiki/Drina" title="Drina">Drina</a> flows through the eastern part of Bosnia, and for the most part it forms a natural border with Serbia.</li> 
        <li>The <a href="/wiki/Neretva" title="Neretva">Neretva</a> is the major river of Herzegovina and the only major river that flows south, into the Adriatic Sea.</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" class="mw-redirect" title="Biodiversity of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Biodiversity of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Phytogeography" title="Phytogeography">Phytogeographically</a>, Bosnia and Herzegovina belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Boreal_Kingdom" title="Boreal Kingdom">Boreal Kingdom</a> and is shared between the Illyrian province of the <a href="/wiki/Circumboreal_Region" title="Circumboreal Region">Circumboreal Region</a> and Adriatic province of the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Basin" title="Mediterranean Basin">Mediterranean Region</a>. According to the <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Fund_for_Nature" title="World Wide Fund for Nature">World Wide Fund for Nature</a>, the territory of Bosnia and Herzegovina can be subdivided into four <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">ecoregions</a>: <a href="/wiki/Balkan_mixed_forests" title="Balkan mixed forests">Balkan mixed forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dinaric_Mountains_mixed_forests" title="Dinaric Mountains mixed forests">Dinaric Mountains mixed forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pannonian_mixed_forests" title="Pannonian mixed forests">Pannonian mixed forests</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Illyrian_deciduous_forests" title="Illyrian deciduous forests">Illyrian deciduous forests</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-105">[103]</a></sup> The country had a 2018 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 5.99/10, ranking it 89<sup>th</sup> globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-106">[104]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:1208px">
       <div class="thumbinner">
        <div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Neum,_panoramatick%C3%BD_pohled.jpg" class="image" title="Panoramic view towards Neum, Bosnia and Herzegovina's 20&nbsp;km (12&nbsp;mi) of coastline access to the Adriatic Sea."><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Neum%2C_panoramatick%C3%BD_pohled.jpg/1200px-Neum%2C_panoramatick%C3%BD_pohled.jpg" decoding="async" width="1200" height="188" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Neum%2C_panoramatick%C3%BD_pohled.jpg/1800px-Neum%2C_panoramatick%C3%BD_pohled.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Neum%2C_panoramatick%C3%BD_pohled.jpg/2400px-Neum%2C_panoramatick%C3%BD_pohled.jpg 2x" data-file-width="18125" data-file-height="2846"></a>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Neum,_panoramatick%C3%BD_pohled.jpg" title="File:Neum, panoramatickÃ½ pohled.jpg"> </a>
         </div>Panoramic view towards <a href="/wiki/Neum" title="Neum">Neum</a>, Bosnia and Herzegovina's 20&nbsp;km (12&nbsp;mi) of coastline access to the <a href="/wiki/Adriatic_Sea" title="Adriatic Sea">Adriatic Sea</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span></h2> 
      <table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399"></a>
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">

          </div></td>

       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Politics of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Politics of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Political_divisions_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Political divisions of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Political divisions of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Map_Bih_entities.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Map_Bih_entities.png/220px-Map_Bih_entities.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="208" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Map_Bih_entities.png/330px-Map_Bih_entities.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Map_Bih_entities.png/440px-Map_Bih_entities.png 2x" data-file-width="1103" data-file-height="1044"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Map_Bih_entities.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Bosnia and Herzegovina consists of the <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Federation of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Federation of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> (FBiH); <a href="/wiki/Republika_Srpska" title="Republika Srpska">Republika Srpska</a> (RS); and <a href="/wiki/Br%C4%8Dko_District" title="BrÄko District">BrÄko District</a> (BD).
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>As a result of the <a href="/wiki/Dayton_Agreement" title="Dayton Agreement">Dayton Accords</a>, the civilian peace implementation is supervised by the <a href="/wiki/High_Representative_for_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="High Representative for Bosnia and Herzegovina">High Representative for Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> selected by the <a href="/wiki/Peace_Implementation_Council" title="Peace Implementation Council">Peace Implementation Council</a>. The High Representative is the highest political authority in the country. The High Representative has many governmental and legislative powers, including the dismissal of elected and non-elected officials. Due to the vast powers of the High Representative over Bosnian politics and essential <a href="/wiki/Veto" title="Veto">veto</a> powers, the position has also been compared to that of a <a href="/wiki/Viceroy" title="Viceroy">viceroy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[105]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[106]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[107]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[108]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Politics take place in a framework of a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary</a> <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democracy</a>, whereby <a href="/wiki/Executive_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Executive power">executive power</a> is exercised by the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Ministers_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Council of Ministers of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Council of Ministers of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>. <a href="/wiki/Legislative_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative power">Legislative power</a> is vested in both the Council of Ministers and the <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_Assembly_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Parliamentary Assembly of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Parliamentary Assembly of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>. Members of the Parliamentary Assembly are chosen according to a <a href="/wiki/Proportional_representation" title="Proportional representation">proportional representation</a> system.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[109]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[110]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Bosnia and Herzegovina is a <a href="/wiki/Liberal_democracy" title="Liberal democracy">liberal democracy</a>. It has several levels of political structuring, according to the <a href="/wiki/Dayton_Accords" class="mw-redirect" title="Dayton Accords">Dayton Accords</a>. The most important of these levels is the division of the country into two entities: the <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Federation of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Federation of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Republika_Srpska" title="Republika Srpska">Republika Srpska</a>. The Federation of Bosnia and Herzegovina covers 51% of Bosnia and Herzegovina's total area, while Republika Srpska covers 49%. The entities, based largely on the territories held by the two warring sides at the time, were formally established by the Dayton peace agreement in 1995 because of the tremendous changes in Bosnia and Herzegovina's ethnic structure. Since 1996, the power of the entities relative to the State government has decreased significantly. Nonetheless, entities still have numerous powers to themselves. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Br%C4%8Dko_District" title="BrÄko District">BrÄko District</a> in the north of the country was created in 2000, out of land from both entities. It officially belongs to both, but is governed by neither, and functions under a decentralized system of local government. For election purposes, BrÄko District voters can choose to participate in either the Federation or Republika Srpska elections. The BrÄko District has been praised for maintaining a multiethnic population and a level of prosperity significantly above the national average.<sup id="cite_ref-OHR_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OHR-113">[111]</a></sup> </p> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:224px;max-width:224px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:222px;max-width:222px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Parliament_(6042784223).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Parliament_%286042784223%29.jpg/220px-Parliament_%286042784223%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Parliament_%286042784223%29.jpg/330px-Parliament_%286042784223%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Parliament_%286042784223%29.jpg/440px-Parliament_%286042784223%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           Bosnia and Herzegovina's government building in <a href="/wiki/Sarajevo" title="Sarajevo">Sarajevo</a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:222px;max-width:222px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Hipotekarna_banka_palata_predsjednika.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Hipotekarna_banka_palata_predsjednika.JPG/220px-Hipotekarna_banka_palata_predsjednika.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Hipotekarna_banka_palata_predsjednika.JPG/330px-Hipotekarna_banka_palata_predsjednika.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Hipotekarna_banka_palata_predsjednika.JPG/440px-Hipotekarna_banka_palata_predsjednika.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1328"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_the_Republic,_Banja_Luka" title="Palace of the Republic, Banja Luka">Palace of the Republic</a> in Banja Luka
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The third level of Bosnia and Herzegovina's political subdivision is manifested in <a href="/wiki/Cantons_of_the_Federation_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Cantons of the Federation of Bosnia and Herzegovina">cantons</a>. They are unique to the Federation of Bosnia and Herzegovina entity, which consists of ten of them. Each has a cantonal government, which is under the law of the Federation as a whole. Some cantons are ethnically mixed and have special laws to ensure the equality of all constituent people.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The fourth level of political division in Bosnia and Herzegovina is the municipality. The Federation of Bosnia and Herzegovina is divided into 74 municipalities, and Republika Srpska into 63. Municipalities also have their own local government, and are typically based on the most significant city or place in their territory. As such, many municipalities have a long tradition and history with their present boundaries. Some others, however, were only created following the recent war after traditional municipalities were split by the <a href="/wiki/Inter-Entity_Boundary_Line" title="Inter-Entity Boundary Line">Inter-Entity Boundary Line</a>. Each canton in the Federation of Bosnia and Herzegovina consists of several municipalities, which are divided into local communities.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Besides entities, cantons, and municipalities, Bosnia and Herzegovina also has four "official" cities. These are: <a href="/wiki/Banja_Luka" title="Banja Luka">Banja Luka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mostar" title="Mostar">Mostar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sarajevo" title="Sarajevo">Sarajevo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Isto%C4%8Dno_Sarajevo" title="IstoÄno Sarajevo">East Sarajevo</a>. The territory and government of the cities of Banja Luka and Mostar corresponds to the municipalities of the same name, while the cities of Sarajevo and East Sarajevo officially consist of several municipalities. Cities have their own city government whose power is in between that of the municipalities and cantons (or the entity, in the case of Republika Srpska). </p>
      <p>More recently, several central institutions have been established (such as <a href="/wiki/Defence_minister" title="Defence minister">defense ministry</a>, security ministry, state court, <a href="/wiki/Indirect_tax" title="Indirect tax">indirect taxation</a> service and so on) in the process of transferring part of the jurisdiction from the entities to the state. The representation of the government of Bosnia and Herzegovina is by elites who represent the country's three major groups, with each having a guaranteed share of power. </p>
      <p>The Chair of the <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Presidency of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Presidency of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> rotates among three members (<a href="/wiki/Bosniaks" title="Bosniaks">Bosniak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serbs" title="Serbs">Serb</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croats" title="Croats">Croat</a>), each elected as the Chair for an eight-month term within their four-year term as a member. The three members of the <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Presidency of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Presidency</a> are elected directly by the people with Federation voters voting for the Bosniak and the Croat, and the <a href="/wiki/Republika_Srpska" title="Republika Srpska">Republika Srpska</a> voters for the Serb. </p>
      <p>The Chair of the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Ministers_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Council of Ministers of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Council of Ministers</a> is nominated by the Presidency and approved by the House of Representatives. He or she is then responsible for appointing a Foreign Minister, Minister of Foreign Trade, and others as appropriate. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_Assembly_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Parliamentary Assembly of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Parliamentary Assembly</a> is the lawmaking body in Bosnia and Herzegovina. It consists of two houses: the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Peoples_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="House of Peoples of Bosnia and Herzegovina">House of Peoples</a> and the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Representatives_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="House of Representatives of Bosnia and Herzegovina">House of Representatives</a>. The House of Peoples has 15 delegates chosen by parliaments of the entities, two-thirds of which come from the Federation (5 Croat and 5 Bosniaks) and one-third from the Republika Srpska (5 Serbs). The House of Representatives is composed of 42 Members elected by the people under a form of <a href="/wiki/Proportional_representation" title="Proportional representation">proportional representation</a> (PR), two-thirds elected from the Federation and one-third elected from the Republika Srpska.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The Constitutional Court of Bosnia and Herzegovina is the supreme, final arbiter of legal matters. It is composed of nine members: four members are selected by the House of Representatives of the Federation, two by the Assembly of the Republika Srpska, and three by the President of the <a href="/wiki/European_Court_of_Human_Rights" title="European Court of Human Rights">European Court of Human Rights</a> after consultation with the Presidency, but cannot be Bosnian citizens.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>However, the highest political authority in the country is the High Representative in Bosnia and Herzegovina, the chief <a href="/wiki/Executive_officer" title="Executive officer">executive officer</a> for the international civilian presence in the country and is selected by the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>. Since 1995, the High Representative has been able to bypass the elected parliamentary assembly, and since 1997 has been able to remove elected officials. The methods selected by the High Representative have been criticized as undemocratic.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[112]</a></sup> International supervision is to end when the country is deemed politically and democratically stable and self-sustaining. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h3> 
      <table class="box-One_source plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-one_source" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="Question book-new.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399"></a>
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">
           This section <b>relies largely or entirely on a single <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Reliable sources">source</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Relevant discussion may be found on the <a href="/wiki/Talk:Bosnia_and_Herzegovina##" title="Talk:Bosnia and Herzegovina">talk page</a>. Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bosnia_and_Herzegovina&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by introducing <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">citations</a> to additional sources.<br><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Bosnia+and+Herzegovina%22">"Bosnia and Herzegovina"</a>&nbsp;â&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Bosnia+and+Herzegovina%22+-wikipedia">news</a>&nbsp;<b>Â·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Bosnia+and+Herzegovina%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers">newspapers</a>&nbsp;<b>Â·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Bosnia+and+Herzegovina%22+-wikipedia">books</a>&nbsp;<b>Â·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Bosnia+and+Herzegovina%22">scholar</a>&nbsp;<b>Â·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Bosnia+and+Herzegovina%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on">JSTOR</a></span></small></span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">March 2018</span>)</i></small>
          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Armed_Forces_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Armed Forces of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Armed Forces of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> (OSBiH) were unified into a single entity in 2005, with the merger of the <a href="/wiki/Army_of_the_Federation_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Army of the Federation of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Army of the Federation of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Army_of_Republika_Srpska" title="Army of Republika Srpska">Army of Republika Srpska</a>, which had defended their respective regions. The <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defense_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" class="mw-redirect" title="Ministry of Defense of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Ministry of Defense</a> was founded in 2004. </p>
      <p>The Bosnian military consists of the <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_Ground_Forces" class="mw-redirect" title="Bosnian Ground Forces">Bosnian Ground Forces</a> and <a href="/wiki/Air_Force_and_Anti-Aircraft_Defence_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Air Force and Anti-Aircraft Defence of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Air Force and Air Defense</a>. The Ground Forces number 7,200 active and 5,000 reserve personnel. They are armed with a mix of American, Yugoslavian, Soviet, and European-made weaponry, vehicles, and military equipment. The Air Force and Air Defense Forces have 1,500 personnel and about 62 aircraft. The Air Defense Forces operate <a href="/wiki/MANPADS" class="mw-redirect" title="MANPADS">MANPADS</a> hand-held missiles, <a href="/wiki/Surface-to-air_missile" title="Surface-to-air missile">surface-to-air missile</a> (SAM) batteries, anti-aircraft cannons, and radar. The Army has recently adopted remodeled <a href="/wiki/MARPAT" title="MARPAT">MARPAT</a> uniforms, used by Bosnian soldiers serving with <a href="/wiki/ISAF" class="mw-redirect" title="ISAF">ISAF</a> in <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>. A domestic production program is now underway to ensure that army units are equipped with the correct ammunition. </p>
      <p>Beginning in 2007, the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" class="mw-redirect" title="Ministry of Defence of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Ministry of Defence of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> undertook the army's first ever international assistance mission, enlisting the military to serve with ISAF peace missions to Afghanistan, <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_Congo" class="mw-redirect" title="Democratic Republic of Congo">Democratic Republic of Congo</a> in 2007. Five officers, acting as officers/advisors, served in the Democratic Republic of Congo. 45 soldiers, mostly acting as base security and medical assistants, served in Afghanistan. 85 Bosnian soldiers served as base security in Iraq, occasionally conducting infantry patrols there as well. All three deployed groups have been commended by their respective international forces as well as the Ministry of Defence of Bosnia and Herzegovina. The international assistance operations are still ongoing. </p>
      <p>The Air Force and Anti-Aircraft Defence Brigade of Bosnia and Herzegovina was formed when elements of the <a href="/wiki/Army_of_the_Federation_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Army of the Federation of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Army of the Federation of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Republika_Srpska_Air_Force" title="Republika Srpska Air Force">Republika Srpska Air Force</a> were merged in 2006. The Air Force has seen improvements in the last few years with added funds for aircraft repairs and improved cooperation with the <a href="/wiki/Ground_Forces" class="mw-redirect" title="Ground Forces">Ground Forces</a> as well as to the citizens of the country. The Ministry of Defense of Bosnia and Herzegovina is pursuing the acquisition of new aircraft including helicopters and perhaps even fighter jets.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[113]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Foreign relations of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Foreign relations of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Bosnia and Herzegovina to the European Union">Accession of Bosnia and Herzegovina to the European Union</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Bosnia and Herzegovina to the European Union">EU integration</a> is one of the main political objectives of Bosnia and Herzegovina; it initiated the <a href="/wiki/Stabilisation_and_Association_Process" title="Stabilisation and Association Process">Stabilisation and Association Process</a> in 2007. Countries participating in the SAP have been offered the possibility to become, once they fulfill the necessary conditions, Member States of the EU. Bosnia and Herzegovina is therefore a potential candidate country for EU accession.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[114]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The implementation of the <a href="/wiki/Dayton_Agreement" title="Dayton Agreement">Dayton Accords</a> of 1995 has focused the efforts of policymakers in Bosnia and Herzegovina, as well as the international community, on regional stabilization in the countries-successors of the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">former Yugoslavia</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Within Bosnia and Herzegovina, relations with its neighbors of <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a> have been fairly stable since the signing of the <a href="/wiki/Dayton_Agreement" title="Dayton Agreement">Dayton Agreement</a> in 1995. On 23 April 2010, Bosnia and Herzegovina received the <a href="/wiki/Membership_Action_Plan" class="mw-redirect" title="Membership Action Plan">Membership Action Plan</a> from <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>, which is the last step before full membership in the alliance. Full membership was expected in 2014 or 2015, depending on the progress of reforms.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[115]</a></sup> In December 2018, NATO approved a Bosnian Membership Action Plan.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[116]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Demographics of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Demographics of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Demographic_history_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Demographic history of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Demographic history of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>
      </div> 
      <p>According to the <a href="/wiki/1991_population_census_in_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="1991 population census in Bosnia and Herzegovina">1991 census</a>, Bosnia and Herzegovina had a population of 4,369,319, while the 1996 World Bank Group census showed a decrease to 3,764,425.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[117]</a></sup> Large population migrations during the Yugoslav wars in the 1990s have caused demographic shifts in the country. Between 1991 and 2013, political disagreements made it impossible to organize a census. A census had been planned for 2011,<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[118]</a></sup> and then for 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[119]</a></sup> but was delayed until October 2013. The <a href="/wiki/2013_population_census_in_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="2013 population census in Bosnia and Herzegovina">2013 census</a> found a total population of 3,531,159 people,<sup id="cite_ref-Popis2013_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Popis2013-6">[6]</a></sup> a drop of approximately 20% since 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[120]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span></h3>

      <p>Bosnia and Herzegovina is home to three ethnic "<a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Ethnic groups in Bosnia and Herzegovina">constituent peoples</a>", namely <a href="/wiki/Bosniaks" title="Bosniaks">Bosniaks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serbs" title="Serbs">Serbs</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Croats" title="Croats">Croats</a>, plus a number of smaller groups including <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="History of the Jews in Bosnia and Herzegovina">Jews</a> and <a href="/wiki/Romani_people_in_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Romani people in Bosnia and Herzegovina">Roma</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[121]</a></sup> According to data from <a href="/wiki/2013_population_census_in_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="2013 population census in Bosnia and Herzegovina">2013 census</a> published by the Agency for Statistics of Bosnia and Herzegovina, Bosniaks constitute 50.1% of the population, Serbs 30.8%, Croats 15.5% and others 2.7%, with the remaining respondents not declaring their ethnicity or not answering.<sup id="cite_ref-Popis2013_6-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Popis2013-6">[6]</a></sup> The census results are contested by the Republika Srpska statistical office and by Bosnian Serb politicians.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[122]</a></sup> The dispute over the census concerns the inclusion of non-permanent Bosnian residents in the figures, which Republika Srpska officials oppose.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[123]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>'s statistics office, <a href="/wiki/Eurostat" title="Eurostat">Eurostat</a>, concluded in May 2016 that the census methodology used by the Bosnian statistical agency is in line with international recommendations.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[124]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3> 
      <p>Bosnia's constitution does not specify any official languages.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[125]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[126]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Footitt_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Footitt-129">[127]</a></sup> However, academics Hilary Footitt and Michael Kelly note the Dayton Agreement states it is "done in <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_language" title="Bosnian language">Bosnian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croatian_language" title="Croatian language">Croatian</a>, English and <a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">Serbian</a>", and they describe this as the "de facto recognition of three official languages" at the state level. The equal status of Bosnian, Serbian and Croatian was verified by the Constitutional Court in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-Footitt_129-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Footitt-129">[127]</a></sup> It ruled the provisions of the Federation and Republika Srpska constitutions on language were incompatible with the state constitution, since they only recognised "Bosniak" and Croatian (in the case of the Federation) and Serbian (in the case of Republika Srpska) as official languages at the entity level. As a result, the wording of the entity constitutions was changed and all three languages were made official in both entities.<sup id="cite_ref-Footitt_129-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Footitt-129">[127]</a></sup> The three <a href="/wiki/Standard_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Standard languages">standard languages</a> are fully <a href="/wiki/Mutual_intelligibility" title="Mutual intelligibility">mutually intelligible</a> and are known collectively under the appellation of <a href="/wiki/Serbo-Croatian" title="Serbo-Croatian">Serbo-Croatian</a>, despite this term not being formally recognized in the country. Use of one of the three languages has become a marker of ethnic identity.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[128]</a></sup> Michael Kelly and Catherine Baker argue: "The three official languages of today's Bosnian state...represent the symbolic assertion of national identity over the pragmatism of mutual intelligibility".<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[129]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to the 1992 <a href="/wiki/European_Charter_for_Regional_or_Minority_Languages" title="European Charter for Regional or Minority Languages">European Charter for Regional or Minority Languages</a>, Bosnia and Herzegovina recognizes the following minority languages: <a href="/wiki/Albanian_language" title="Albanian language">Albanian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montenegrin_language" title="Montenegrin language">Montenegrin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">Czech</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">Hungarian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_language" title="Macedonian language">Macedonian</a>, <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">Polish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romani_language" title="Romani language">Romani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romanian_language" title="Romanian language">Romanian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rusyn_language" title="Rusyn language">Rusyn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovak_language" title="Slovak language">Slovak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovene_language" title="Slovene language">Slovene</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_language" title="Ukrainian language">Ukrainian</a> and Jewish (<a href="/wiki/Yiddish" title="Yiddish">Yiddish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Judaeo-Spanish" title="Judaeo-Spanish">Ladino</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-charter-ratifications_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-charter-ratifications-132">[130]</a></sup> The German minority in Bosnia and Herzegovina are mostly remnants of <a href="/wiki/Donauschwaben" class="mw-redirect" title="Donauschwaben">Donauschwaben</a> (Danube Swabians), who settled in the area after the <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Empire" title="Austrian Empire">Habsburg monarchy</a> claimed the Balkans from the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>. Due to <a href="/wiki/Flight_and_expulsion_of_Germans" class="mw-redirect" title="Flight and expulsion of Germans">expulsions</a> and <a href="/wiki/Organised_persecution_of_ethnic_Germans" class="mw-redirect" title="Organised persecution of ethnic Germans">(forced) assimilation</a> after the two <a href="/wiki/World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="World War">World Wars</a>, the number of ethnic Germans in Bosnia and Herzegovina was drastically diminished.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[131]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In a 2013 census, 52.86% of the population consider their mother tongue Bosnian, 30.76% Serbian, 14.6% Croatian and 1.57% another language, with 0.21% not giving an answer.<sup id="cite_ref-Popis2013_6-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Popis2013-6">[6]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3>

       </div> 
      </div> 
      <p>Bosnia and Herzegovina is a religiously diverse country. According to the census of 2013, <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Muslims</a> comprised 50.7% of the population, while <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Orthodox Christians</a> made 30.7%, Catholics 15.2%, 1.2% other and 1.1% atheist or agnostic, with the remainder not declaring or not answering the question.<sup id="cite_ref-Popis2013_6-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Popis2013-6">[6]</a></sup> A 2012 survey found 54% of Bosnia's <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslims</a> were <a href="/wiki/Non-denominational_Muslim" title="Non-denominational Muslim">non-denominational</a>, while 38% followed <a href="/wiki/Sunnism" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunnism">Sunnism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[132]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cities">Cities</span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Sarajevo" title="Sarajevo">Sarajevo</a> is home to 419,957 inhabitants in its urban area which comprises the <a href="/wiki/Sarajevo#Municipalities_and_city_government" title="Sarajevo">City of Sarajevo</a> as well as municipalities of <a href="/wiki/Ilid%C5%BEa" title="IlidÅ¾a">IlidÅ¾a</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vogo%C5%A1%C4%87a" title="VogoÅ¡Äa">VogoÅ¡Äa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Isto%C4%8Dna_Ilid%C5%BEa" title="IstoÄna IlidÅ¾a">IstoÄna IlidÅ¾a</a>, <a href="/wiki/Isto%C4%8Dno_Novo_Sarajevo" title="IstoÄno Novo Sarajevo">IstoÄno Novo Sarajevo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Isto%C4%8Dni_Stari_Grad" title="IstoÄni Stari Grad">IstoÄni Stari Grad</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[133]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Sarajevo_metropolitan_area" title="Sarajevo metropolitan area">metro area</a> has a population of 555,210 and includes <a href="/wiki/Sarajevo_Canton" title="Sarajevo Canton">Sarajevo Canton</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_Sarajevo" class="mw-redirect" title="East Sarajevo">East Sarajevo</a> and municipalities <a href="/wiki/Breza,_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Breza, Bosnia and Herzegovina">Breza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kiseljak" title="Kiseljak">Kiseljak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kre%C5%A1evo" title="KreÅ¡evo">KreÅ¡evo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Visoko" title="Visoko">Visoko</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (October 2020)">dubious</span></a> <span class="metadata"> â <a href="/wiki/Talk:Bosnia_and_Herzegovina#Dubious" title="Talk:Bosnia and Herzegovina">discuss</a></span></i>]</sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Economy of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Economy of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_companies_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="List of companies of Bosnia and Herzegovina">List of companies of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Tree_map_export_2009_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina.jpeg/220px-Tree_map_export_2009_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina.jpeg" decoding="async" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Tree_map_export_2009_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina.jpeg/330px-Tree_map_export_2009_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Tree_map_export_2009_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina.jpeg/440px-Tree_map_export_2009_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="1105" data-file-height="865"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Graphical depiction of Bosnia and Herzegovina's product exports in 28 color-coded categories
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>During the <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_War" title="Bosnian War">Bosnian War</a>, the economy suffered â¬200&nbsp;billion in material damages.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[135]</a></sup> Bosnia and Herzegovina faces the dual-problem of rebuilding a war-torn country and introducing transitional liberal market reforms to its formerly mixed economy. One legacy of the previous era is a strong industry; under former republic president <a href="/wiki/D%C5%BEemal_Bijedi%C4%87" title="DÅ¾emal BijediÄ">DÅ¾emal BijediÄ</a> and SFRY President <a href="/wiki/Josip_Broz_Tito" title="Josip Broz Tito">Josip Broz Tito</a>, metal industries were promoted in the republic, resulting in the development of a large share of Yugoslavia's plants; S.R. Bosnia and Herzegovina had a very strong industrial export oriented economy in the 1970s and 1980s, with large scale exports worth millions of <a href="/wiki/US$" class="mw-redirect" title="US$">US$</a>. </p>
      <p>For most of Bosnia's history, agriculture has been conducted on privately owned farms; Fresh food has traditionally been exported from the republic.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[136]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The war in the 1990s, caused a dramatic change in the Bosnian economy.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[137]</a></sup> GDP fell by 60% and the destruction of physical infrastructure devastated the economy.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[138]</a></sup> With much of the production capacity unrestored, the Bosnian economy still faces considerable difficulties. Figures show GDP and per capita income increased 10% from 2003 to 2004; this and Bosnia's shrinking <a href="/wiki/Government_debt" title="Government debt">national debt</a> being negative trends, and high unemployment 38.7% and a large <a href="/wiki/Balance_of_trade" title="Balance of trade">trade deficit</a> remain cause for concern. </p>
      <p>The national currency is the (Euro-pegged) <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_convertible_mark" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina convertible mark">Convertible Mark</a> (KM), controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Currency_board" title="Currency board">currency board</a>. Annual inflation is the lowest relative to other countries in the region at 1.9% in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[139]</a></sup> The international debt was $5.1&nbsp;billion (as on 31 December 2014). <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">Real GDP</a> growth rate was 5% for 2004 according to the Bosnian <a href="/wiki/Central_Bank_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Central Bank of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Central Bank of BiH</a> and Statistical Office of Bosnia and Herzegovina. </p>
      <p>Bosnia and Herzegovina has displayed positive progress in the previous years, which decisively moved its place from the lowest income equality rank of <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_income_equality" title="List of countries by income equality">income equality rankings</a> fourteen out of 193 nations.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[140]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to <a href="/wiki/Eurostat" title="Eurostat">Eurostat</a> data, Bosnia and Herzegovina's PPS GDP per capita stood at 29 per cent of the EU average in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[141]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> (IMF) announced a loan to Bosnia worth US$500&nbsp;million to be delivered by <a href="/wiki/IMF_Stand-By_Arrangement" title="IMF Stand-By Arrangement">Stand-By Arrangement</a>. This was scheduled to be approved in September 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[142]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The United States Embassy in Sarajevo, Bosnia and Herzegovina produces the Country Commercial Guide â an annual report that delivers a comprehensive look at Bosnia and Herzegovina's commercial and economic environment, using economic, political, and market analysis. It can be viewed on <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20121018193841/http://sarajevo.usembassy.gov/country-commercial-guide.html">Embassy Sarajevo's website</a>. </p>
      <p>By some estimates, <a href="/wiki/Grey_economy" class="mw-redirect" title="Grey economy">grey economy</a> is 25.5% of GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[143]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2017, exports grew by 17% when compared to the previous year, totaling â¬5.65&nbsp;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[144]</a></sup> The total volume of <a href="/wiki/Foreign_trade" class="mw-redirect" title="Foreign trade">foreign trade</a> in 2017 amounted to â¬14.97&nbsp;billion and increased by 14% compared to the previous year. Imports of goods increased by 12% and amounted to â¬9.32&nbsp;billion. The <a href="/wiki/Balance_of_trade" title="Balance of trade">coverage of imports by exports</a> has increased by 3% compared to the previous year and now it is 61 percent. In 2017, Bosnia and Herzegovina mostly exported <a href="/wiki/Car_seat" title="Car seat">car seats</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electricity" title="Electricity">electricity</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wood_processing" title="Wood processing">processed wood</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aluminum" class="mw-redirect" title="Aluminum">aluminum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Furniture" title="Furniture">furniture</a>. In the same year, it mostly imported <a href="/wiki/Crude_oil" class="mw-redirect" title="Crude oil">crude oil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Automobile" class="mw-redirect" title="Automobile">automobiles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Motor_oil" title="Motor oil">motor oil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coal" title="Coal">coal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Briquettes" class="mw-redirect" title="Briquettes">briquettes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[145]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The unemployment rate in 2017 was 20.5%, but The Vienna Institute for International Economic Studies is predicting falling unemployment rate for the next few years. In 2018, the unemployment should be 19.4% and it should further fall to 18.8% in 2019. In 2020, the unemployment rate should go down to 18.3%.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[146]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 31 December 2017, <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Ministers_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Council of Ministers of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Council of Ministers of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> issued the report on public debt of Bosnia and Herzegovina, stating the public debt was reduced by â¬389.97&nbsp;million, or by more than 6% when compared to 31 December 2016. By the end of 2017, public debt was â¬5.92&nbsp;billion, which amounted to 35.6 percent of GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[147]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of 31&nbsp;December&nbsp;2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bosnia_and_Herzegovina&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there were 32,292 registered companies in the country, which together had revenues of â¬33.572&nbsp;billion that same year.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[148]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2017, the country received â¬397.35&nbsp;million in <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">foreign direct investment</a>, which equals to 2.5% of the GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[149]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2017, Bosnia and Herzegovina ranked 3rd in the world in terms of the number of new jobs created by foreign investment, relative to the number of inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[150]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[151]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2018, Bosnia and Herzegovina exported goods worth 11.9&nbsp;billion KM (â¬6.07&nbsp;billion), which is 7.43% higher than in the same period in 2017, while imports amounted to 19.27&nbsp;billion KM (â¬9.83&nbsp;billion), which is 5.47% higher.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[152]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The average price of new apartments sold in the country in the first 6 months of 2018 is 1,639&nbsp;km (â¬886.31) per square meter. This represents a jump of 3.5% from the previous year.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[153]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 30 June 2018, public debt of Bosnia and Herzegovina amounted to about â¬6.04&nbsp;billion, of which external debt is 70.56 percent, while the internal debt is 29.4 percent of total public indebtedness. The share of public debt in gross domestic product is 34.92 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[154]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the first 7 months of 2018, 811,660 tourists visited the country, a 12.2% jump when compared to the first 7 months of 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[155]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the first 11 months of 2018, 1,378,542 tourists visited Bosnia-Herzegovina, an increase of 12.6%, and had 2,871,004 overnight hotel stays, a 13.8% increase from the previous year. Also, 71.8% of the tourists came from foreign countries.<sup id="cite_ref-klix.ba_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-klix.ba-158">[156]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2018, the total value of <a href="/wiki/Mergers_and_acquisitions" title="Mergers and acquisitions">mergers and acquisitions</a> in Bosnia and Herzegovina amounted to â¬404.6&nbsp;million.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[157]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2018, 99.5 percent of enterprises in Bosnia and Herzegovina used computers in their business, while 99.3 percent had internet connections, according to a survey conducted by the Bosnia and Herzegovina Statistics Agency.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[158]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2018, Bosnia and Herzegovina received 783.4&nbsp;million KM (â¬400.64&nbsp;million) in <a href="/wiki/Direct_foreign_investment" class="mw-redirect" title="Direct foreign investment">direct foreign investment</a>, which was equivalent to 2.3% of GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[159]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2018, <a href="/wiki/Central_Bank_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Central Bank of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Central Bank of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> made a profit of 8,430,875&nbsp;km (â¬4,306,347).<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[160]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> predicts that the economy will grow 3.4% in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[161]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Bosnia and Herzegovina was placed 83rd on the <a href="/wiki/Index_of_Economic_Freedom" title="Index of Economic Freedom">Index of Economic Freedom</a> for 2019. The total rating for Bosnia and Herzegovina is 61.9. This position represents some progress relative to the 91st place in 2018. This result is below the regional level, but still above the global average, making Bosnia and Herzegovina a "moderately free" country.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[162]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 31 January 2019, total deposits in Bosnian banks were KM 21.9&nbsp;billion (â¬11.20&nbsp;billion), which represents 61.15% of nominal GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[163]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the second quarter of 2019, the average price of new apartments sold in Bosnia and Herzegovina was 1,606&nbsp;km (â¬821.47) per square meter.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[164]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the first six months of 2019, exports amounted to 5.829&nbsp;billion KM (â¬2.98&nbsp;billion), which is 0.1% less than in the same period of 2018, while imports amounted to 9.779&nbsp;billion KM (â¬5.00&nbsp;billion), which is by 4.5% more than in the same period of the previous year.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[165]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the first seven months of 2019, 906,788 tourists visited the country, a 11.7% jump from the previous year.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[166]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the first six months of 2019, foreign direct investment amounted to 650.1&nbsp;million KM (â¬332.34&nbsp;million).<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[167]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span></h3>
