      <p>According to projections by the <a href="/wiki/World_Tourism_Organization" title="World Tourism Organization">World Tourism Organization</a>, Bosnia and Herzegovina will have the third highest tourism growth rate in the world between 1995 and 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-Newfound_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Newfound-170">[168]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2018, 1.883.772 tourists visited Bosnia-Herzegovina, an increase of 44,1%, and had 3.843.484 overnight hotel stays, a 43.5% increase from the previous year. Also, 71.2% of the tourists came from foreign countries.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[169]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2017, 1,307,319 tourists visited Bosnia and Herzegovina, an increase of 13.7%, and had 2,677,125 overnight hotel stays, a 12.3% increase from the previous year. 71.5% of the tourists came from foreign countries.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[170]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2006, when ranking the best cities in the world, <a href="/wiki/Lonely_Planet" title="Lonely Planet">Lonely Planet</a> placed <a href="/wiki/Sarajevo" title="Sarajevo">Sarajevo</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Capital_(political)" class="mw-redirect" title="Capital (political)">national capital</a><sup id="cite_ref-Constitution_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-1">[1]</a></sup> and host of the <a href="/wiki/1984_Winter_Olympics" title="1984 Winter Olympics">1984 Winter Olympic Games</a>, as #43 on the list.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[171]</a></sup> Tourism in Sarajevo is chiefly focused on historical, religious, and cultural aspects. In 2010, Lonely Planet's "Best in Travel" nominated it as one of the top ten cities to visit that year.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[172]</a></sup> Sarajevo also won travel blog Foxnomad's "Best City to Visit" competition in 2012, beating more than one hundred other cities around the entire world.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[173]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Me%C4%91ugorje" class="mw-redirect" title="MeÄugorje">MeÄugorje</a> has become one of the most popular pilgrimage sites for Christians in the world and has turned into Europe's third most important religious place, where each year more than 1&nbsp;million people visit.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[174]</a></sup> It has been estimated that 30&nbsp;million pilgrims have come to MeÄugorje since the reputed apparitions began in 1981.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters-177">[175]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Bosnia has also become an increasingly popular skiing and <a href="/wiki/Ecotourism" title="Ecotourism">Ecotourism</a> destination. Bosnia and Herzegovina remains one of the last undiscovered natural regions of the southern area of the Alps, with vast tracts of wild and untouched nature attracting adventurers and nature lovers. <a href="/wiki/National_Geographic_(magazine)" class="mw-redirect" title="National Geographic (magazine)">National Geographic magazine</a> named Bosnia and Herzegovina as the best mountain biking adventure destination for 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-test_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-test-178">[176]</a></sup> The central <a href="/wiki/Dinaric_Alps" title="Dinaric Alps">Bosnian Dinaric Alps</a> are favored by hikers and mountaineers, containing both Mediterranean and Alpine climates. <a href="/wiki/Rafting" title="Rafting">Whitewater rafting</a> is somewhat of a <a href="/wiki/National_sport" title="National sport">national pastime</a>, with three rivers, including the deepest <a href="/wiki/Canyon" title="Canyon">river canyon</a> in Europe, the <a href="/wiki/Tara_River_Canyon" title="Tara River Canyon">Tara River Canyon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Newfound_170-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Newfound-170">[168]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Most recently, the <i><a href="/wiki/Huffington_Post" class="mw-redirect" title="Huffington Post">Huffington Post</a></i> named Bosnia and Herzegovina the "9th Greatest Adventure in the World for 2013", adding that the country boasts "the cleanest water and air in Europe; the greatest untouched forests; and the most wildlife. The best way to experience is the three rivers trip, which purls through the best the Balkans have to offer."<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[177]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Attractions">Attractions</span></h4> 
      <table class="box-Prose plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-style ambox-Prose" role="presentation">

          </div></td>

      <p>Some of the tourist attractions in Bosnia and Herzegovina include: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Sarajevo" title="Sarajevo">Sarajevo</a>, the "Olympic City" or "European Jerusalem"; the scientific, cultural, tourist and commercial center of Bosnia and Herzegovina as well as its capital</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Vratnik_(Sarajevo)" title="Vratnik (Sarajevo)">Vratnik</a> old town and <a href="/wiki/Bijela_Tabija" title="Bijela Tabija">Bijela Tabija</a> fortress in Sarajevo</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Medjugorje" title="Medjugorje">Shrine of Our Lady of MeÄugorje</a>, with Annual Youth Festival; the site of a <a href="/wiki/Marian_apparition" title="Marian apparition">Marian apparition</a> and subsequent Catholic pilgrimage destination</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Mostar" title="Mostar">Mostar</a>, the "City on Neretva" or "City of Sunshine"; the location of the <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Sites</a> of <a href="/wiki/Stari_most" class="mw-redirect" title="Stari most">Stari most</a> and old-town Mostar</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Vi%C5%A1egrad" title="ViÅ¡egrad">ViÅ¡egrad</a>, location of the UNESCO World Heritage Site of the <a href="/wiki/Mehmed_Pa%C5%A1a_Sokolovi%C4%87_Bridge" title="Mehmed PaÅ¡a SokoloviÄ Bridge">Mehmed PaÅ¡a SokoloviÄ Bridge</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Banja_Luka" title="Banja Luka">Banja Luka</a>, the "Green City", with sights such as the Kastel fortress and <a href="/wiki/Ferhat_Pasha_Mosque" title="Ferhat Pasha Mosque">Ferhadija mosque</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Biha%C4%87" title="BihaÄ">BihaÄ</a> and the waterfalls of the river <a href="/wiki/Una_(Sava)" title="Una (Sava)">Una</a> within Una National Park</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Jajce" title="Jajce">Jajce</a>, city of the Bosnian kings and the place where the Federal People's Republic of Yugoslavia was founded, Pliva lakes and waterfall</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Prijedor" title="Prijedor">Prijedor</a>, featuring its Old City Mosque, <a href="/wiki/Kozara_National_Park" title="Kozara National Park">Kozara National Park</a> and, at Mrakovica, Bosnia's largest World War II monument</li> 
       <li>The salt-lakes of <a href="/wiki/Tuzla" title="Tuzla">Tuzla</a>, birthplace of <a href="/wiki/Me%C5%A1a_Selimovi%C4%87" title="MeÅ¡a SelimoviÄ">MeÅ¡a SelimoviÄ</a></li> 
       <li>The <a href="/wiki/Neretva" title="Neretva">Neretva</a> river and the <a href="/wiki/Rakitnica" title="Rakitnica">Rakitnica</a> river canyons in <a href="/wiki/Neretva" title="Neretva">Upper Neretva</a></li> 
       <li>The <a href="/wiki/Trebi%C5%BEat_(river)" title="TrebiÅ¾at (river)">TrebiÅ¾at</a> river and its waterfalls at <a href="/wiki/Kravica_(waterfall)" title="Kravica (waterfall)">Kravica</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ko%C4%87u%C5%A1a" class="mw-redirect" title="KoÄuÅ¡a">KoÄuÅ¡a</a></li> 
       <li>The <a href="/wiki/Buna_(Neretva)" title="Buna (Neretva)">Buna</a> with its spring and historic town of <a href="/wiki/Vrelo_Bune" title="Vrelo Bune">Blagaj</a></li> 
       <li>The <a href="/wiki/Tara_(Drina)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tara (Drina)">Lower Tara</a> river canyon, the deepest canyon in Europe</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Sutjeska_National_Park" title="Sutjeska National Park">Sutjeska National Park</a>, featuring the <a href="/wiki/Old-growth_forest" title="Old-growth forest">ancient forest</a> of <a href="/wiki/Peru%C4%87ica" title="PeruÄica">PeruÄica</a> and the Sutjeska river canyon</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Po%C4%8Ditelj_(%C4%8Capljina)" class="mw-redirect" title="PoÄitelj (Äapljina)">PoÄitelj</a> historical village</li> 
       <li>Mount <a href="/wiki/Bjela%C5%A1nica_Mountain" class="mw-redirect" title="BjelaÅ¡nica Mountain">BjelaÅ¡nica</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jahorina" title="Jahorina">Jahorina</a>, sites used during <a href="/wiki/1984_Winter_Olympics" title="1984 Winter Olympics">XIV Olympic Winter Games in 1984</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Neum" title="Neum">Neum</a>, the only coastal city in Bosnia and Herzegovina with direct access to the Adriatic Sea</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Doboj" title="Doboj">Doboj</a> and its 13th-century fortress</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Stolac_Municipality" class="mw-redirect" title="Stolac Municipality">Stolac</a>, featuring the <a href="/wiki/Begovina" class="mw-redirect" title="Begovina">Begovina</a> neighborhood and <a href="/wiki/Radimlja" title="Radimlja">Radimlja</a> tombstones</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Visoko,_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" class="mw-redirect" title="Visoko, Bosnia and Herzegovina">Visoko</a>, city of the Bosnian nobility and monarchy, historical capital of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Bosnia" title="Kingdom of Bosnia">Kingdom of Bosnia</a> and the site of the alleged <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_pyramids" class="mw-redirect" title="Bosnian pyramids">Bosnian pyramids</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Proko%C5%A1ko_Lake" title="ProkoÅ¡ko Lake">ProkoÅ¡ko Lake</a> in Fojnica</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Te%C5%A1anj" title="TeÅ¡anj">TeÅ¡anj</a>, one of Bosnia's <a href="/wiki/List_of_oldest_continuously_inhabited_cities" title="List of oldest continuously inhabited cities">oldest known cities</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Bijeljina" title="Bijeljina">Bijeljina</a>, known for its agriculture and ethnic village StaniÅ¡iÄ</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Lukavac" title="Lukavac">Lukavac</a>, featuring <a href="/wiki/Modrac_Lake" title="Modrac Lake">Modrac Lake</a>, the largest artificial lake in Bosnia and Herzegovina</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Travnik" title="Travnik">Travnik</a>, the birthplace of <a href="/wiki/Ivo_Andri%C4%87" title="Ivo AndriÄ">Ivo AndriÄ</a> and once the capital city of the <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_Eyalet" title="Bosnia Eyalet">Bosnia Eyalet</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Jablanica,_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Jablanica, Bosnia and Herzegovina">Jablanica</a>, Museum of <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Neretva" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Neretva">Battle of Neretva</a> and Old bridge destroyed by Yugoslav army in <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Ostro%C5%BEac_Castle" title="OstroÅ¾ac Castle">OstroÅ¾ac Castle</a>, a 16th-century castle built by the Ottoman Empire and later expanded by the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Habsburg" title="House of Habsburg">House of Habsburg</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Konjic" title="Konjic">Konjic</a>, featuring Tito's underground nuclear bunker<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[178]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Drvar" title="Drvar">Drvar</a>, featuring Tito's cave and great natural landscapes</li>
      </ul> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Transport in Bosnia and Herzegovina">Transport in Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bh_air_fleet.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Bh_air_fleet.jpg/220px-Bh_air_fleet.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Bh_air_fleet.jpg/330px-Bh_air_fleet.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Bh_air_fleet.jpg/440px-Bh_air_fleet.jpg 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="540"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bh_air_fleet.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Apron overview of Sarajevo International Airport
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Sarajevo_International_Airport" title="Sarajevo International Airport">Sarajevo International Airport</a> (<a href="/wiki/IATA_airport_code" title="IATA airport code">IATA</a>: <b>SJJ</b>, <a href="/wiki/ICAO_airport_code" title="ICAO airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>LQSA</b>), also known as <i>Butmir Airport</i>, is the main <a href="/wiki/International_airport" title="International airport">international airport</a> in Bosnia and Herzegovina, located 3.3&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Nautical_mile" title="Nautical mile">NM</a> (6.1&nbsp;km; 3.8&nbsp;mi) southwest of the <a href="/wiki/Sarajevo_main_railway_station" title="Sarajevo main railway station">Sarajevo main railway station</a><sup id="cite_ref-AIP_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AIP-181">[179]</a></sup> in the city of <a href="/wiki/Sarajevo" title="Sarajevo">Sarajevo</a> in the suburb of <a href="/wiki/Butmir" title="Butmir">Butmir</a>. </p>
      <p>Railway operations in Bosnia and Herzegovina are successors of the <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_Railways" title="Yugoslav Railways">Yugoslav Railways</a> within the country boundaries following independence from the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Former Yugoslavia</a> in 1992. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Telecommunications">Telecommunications</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_in_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Telecommunications in Bosnia and Herzegovina">Telecommunications in Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The Bosnian communications market was fully liberalised in January 2006. There are three <a href="/wiki/Landline" title="Landline">landline</a> telephone providers, although each one predominantly serves a partile services are provided by three operators, with nationwide services. Mobile data services are also available, including high-speed <a href="/wiki/Enhanced_Data_Rates_for_GSM_Evolution" title="Enhanced Data Rates for GSM Evolution">EDGE</a> and <a href="/wiki/3G" title="3G">3G</a> services.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[180]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><i><a href="/wiki/Oslobo%C4%91enje" title="OsloboÄenje">OsloboÄenje</a></i> (Liberation), founded in 1943, is one of the country's longest running continuously circulating newspapers. There are many national publications, only some of which include the <i><a href="/wiki/Dnevni_Avaz" class="mw-redirect" title="Dnevni Avaz">Dnevni Avaz</a></i> (Daily Voice), founded in 1995, and <i>Jutarnje Novine</i> (Morning News) in circulation in Sarajevo.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[181]</a></sup> Other local periodicals include the Croatian newspaper <a href="/wiki/Hrvatska_rije%C4%8D" title="Hrvatska rijeÄ">Hrvatska rijeÄ</a> and the Bosnian magazine <a href="/wiki/Start_(newspaper)" title="Start (newspaper)">Start</a>, as well as the weekly newspapers <i>Slobodna Bosna</i> (<i>Free Bosnia</i>) and <i>BH Dani</i> (<i>BH Days</i>). <i><a href="/wiki/Novi_Plamen" title="Novi Plamen">Novi Plamen</a></i>, a monthly magazine, is the most left-wing publication. The international news station <a href="/wiki/Al_Jazeera" title="Al Jazeera">Al Jazeera</a> maintains a sister channel that caters to the <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkan</a> region, <a href="/wiki/Al_Jazeera_Balkans" title="Al Jazeera Balkans">Al Jazeera Balkans</a>, broadcasting out of and based in Sarajevo.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[182]</a></sup> Since 2014, the <a href="/wiki/N1_(television)" class="mw-redirect" title="N1 (television)">N1 platform</a> began broadcasting as an affiliate of <a href="/wiki/CNN_International" title="CNN International">CNN International</a> and has headquarters in Sarajevo, Zagreb, and Belgrade.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[183]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Additionally, the country is the most liberal in terms of <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_the_press" title="Freedom of the press">freedom of the press</a> in the region, ranking 43rd internationally.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[184]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of December&nbsp;2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bosnia_and_Herzegovina&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there are 3,064,072 internet users in the country or 86.77% of the entire population.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[185]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Education in Bosnia and Herzegovina">Education in Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sarajevo_University_building.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Sarajevo_University_building.JPG/220px-Sarajevo_University_building.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Sarajevo_University_building.JPG/330px-Sarajevo_University_building.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Sarajevo_University_building.JPG/440px-Sarajevo_University_building.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sarajevo_University_building.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Sarajevo" title="University of Sarajevo">University of Sarajevo</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Sarajevo_Law_School" class="mw-redirect" title="Sarajevo Law School">Faculty of Law</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Higher education has a long and rich tradition in Bosnia and Herzegovina. The first bespoke higher-education institution was a school of <a href="/wiki/Sufism" title="Sufism">Sufi</a> philosophy established by <a href="/wiki/Gazi_Husrev-beg" title="Gazi Husrev-beg">Gazi Husrev-beg</a> in 1531. Numerous other religious schools then followed. In 1887, under the Austro-Hungarian Empire, a <a href="/wiki/Sharia" title="Sharia">Sharia</a> law school began a five-year program.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[186]</a></sup> In the 1940s the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Sarajevo" title="University of Sarajevo">University of Sarajevo</a> became the city's first secular higher education institute. In the 1950s post-bachelaurate graduate degrees became available.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[187]</a></sup> Severely damaged during the war, it was recently rebuilt in partnership with more than 40 other universities. There are various other institutions of higher education, including: <a href="/wiki/University_%22D%C5%BEemal_Bijedi%C4%87%22_of_Mostar" class="mw-redirect" title="University &quot;DÅ¾emal BijediÄ&quot; of Mostar">University "DÅ¾emal BijediÄ" of Mostar</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Banja_Luka" title="University of Banja Luka">University of Banja Luka</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Mostar" title="University of Mostar">University of Mostar</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_East_Sarajevo" title="University of East Sarajevo">University of East Sarajevo</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Tuzla" title="University of Tuzla">University of Tuzla</a>, <a href="/wiki/American_University_in_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="American University in Bosnia and Herzegovina">American University in Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Sciences_and_Arts_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Academy of Sciences and Arts of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Academy of Sciences and Arts of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>, which is held in high regard as one of the most prestigious creative arts academies in the region. </p>
      <p>Also, Bosnia and Herzegovina is home to several private and international higher education institutions, some of which are: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Sarajevo_School_of_Science_and_Technology" title="Sarajevo School of Science and Technology">Sarajevo School of Science and Technology</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/International_University_of_Sarajevo" title="International University of Sarajevo">International University of Sarajevo</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/American_University_in_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="American University in Bosnia and Herzegovina">American University in Bosnia and Herzegovina</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Sarajevo_Graduate_School_of_Business" title="Sarajevo Graduate School of Business">Sarajevo Graduate School of Business</a></li> 
       <li>International Burch University</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Primary schooling lasts for nine years. Secondary education is provided by general and technical secondary schools (typically <a href="/wiki/Gymnasium_(school)" title="Gymnasium (school)">Gymnasiums</a>) where studies typically last for four years. All forms of secondary schooling include an element of <a href="/wiki/Vocational_education" title="Vocational education">vocational training</a>. Pupils graduating from general secondary schools obtain the <a href="/wiki/Matura" title="Matura">Matura</a> and can enroll in any tertiary educational institution or academy by passing a qualification examination prescribed by the governing body or institution. Students graduating technical subjects obtain a <a href="/wiki/Diploma" title="Diploma">Diploma</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[188]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Culture of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Culture of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sarajevo,_knihovna.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Sarajevo%2C_knihovna.jpg/220px-Sarajevo%2C_knihovna.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Sarajevo%2C_knihovna.jpg/330px-Sarajevo%2C_knihovna.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Sarajevo%2C_knihovna.jpg/440px-Sarajevo%2C_knihovna.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4440" data-file-height="3129"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sarajevo,_knihovna.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/National_Library_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" class="mw-redirect" title="National Library of Bosnia and Herzegovina">National Library</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sarajevo" title="Sarajevo">Sarajevo</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Architecture of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Architecture of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The architecture of Bosnia and Herzegovina is largely influenced by four major periods where political and social changes influenced the creation of distinct cultural and architectural habits of the population. Each period made its influence felt and contributed to a greater diversity of cultures and architectural language in this region. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" class="mw-redirect" title="Media of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Media of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Radio_and_Television_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_(BHRT)_building,_Sarajevo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Radio_and_Television_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_%28BHRT%29_building%2C_Sarajevo.jpg/250px-Radio_and_Television_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_%28BHRT%29_building%2C_Sarajevo.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="88" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Radio_and_Television_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_%28BHRT%29_building%2C_Sarajevo.jpg/375px-Radio_and_Television_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_%28BHRT%29_building%2C_Sarajevo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Radio_and_Television_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_%28BHRT%29_building%2C_Sarajevo.jpg/500px-Radio_and_Television_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_%28BHRT%29_building%2C_Sarajevo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4652" data-file-height="1634"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Radio_and_Television_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_(BHRT)_building,_Sarajevo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Radio_and_Television_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Radio and Television of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Radio and Television of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> headquarter in <a href="/wiki/Sarajevo" title="Sarajevo">Sarajevo</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Some television, magazines, and newspapers in Bosnia and Herzegovina are state-owned, and some are for-profit corporations funded by <a href="/wiki/Advertising" title="Advertising">advertising</a>, <a href="/wiki/Subscription" class="mw-redirect" title="Subscription">subscription</a>, and other sales-related revenues. The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Constitution of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Constitution of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> guarantees <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_speech" title="Freedom of speech">freedom of speech</a>. </p>
      <p>As a <a href="/wiki/Country_in_transition" class="mw-redirect" title="Country in transition">country in transition</a> with a post-war legacy and a <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Politics of Bosnia and Herzegovina">complex domestic political structure</a> Bosnia and Herzegovina's media system is under transformation. In the early post-war period (1995â2005), media development was guided mainly by international donors and cooperation agencies, who invested to help reconstruct, diversify, democratize and professionalize media outlets.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[189]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EJC_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EJC-192">[190]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Post-war developments included the establishment of an independent Communication Regulatory Agency, the adoption of a Press Code, the establishment of the Press Council, the decriminalization of label and defamation, the introduction of a rather advanced Freedom of Access to Information Law, and the creation of a Public Service Broadcasting System from the formerly state-owned broadcaster. Yet, internationally backed positive developments have been often obstructed by domestic elites, and the professionalisation of media and journalists has proceeded only slowly. High levels of partisanship and linkages between the media and the political systems hinder the adherence to professional code of conducts.<sup id="cite_ref-EJC_192-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EJC-192">[190]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Literature_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" class="mw-redirect" title="Literature of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Literature of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Bosnia and Herzegovina has a rich literature, including the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_prize" class="mw-redirect" title="Nobel prize">Nobel prize</a> winner <a href="/wiki/Ivo_Andri%C4%87" title="Ivo AndriÄ">Ivo AndriÄ</a> and poets such as <a href="/wiki/Antun_Branko_%C5%A0imi%C4%87" title="Antun Branko Å imiÄ">Antun Branko Å imiÄ</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aleksa_%C5%A0anti%C4%87" title="Aleksa Å antiÄ">Aleksa Å antiÄ</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jovan_Du%C4%8Di%C4%87" title="Jovan DuÄiÄ">Jovan DuÄiÄ</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mak_Dizdar" title="Mak Dizdar">Mak Dizdar</a>, writers such as <a href="/wiki/Zlatko_Top%C4%8Di%C4%87" title="Zlatko TopÄiÄ">Zlatko TopÄiÄ</a>, <a href="/wiki/Me%C5%A1a_Selimovi%C4%87" title="MeÅ¡a SelimoviÄ">MeÅ¡a SelimoviÄ</a>, <a href="/wiki/Semezdin_Mehmedinovi%C4%87" title="Semezdin MehmedinoviÄ">Semezdin MehmedinoviÄ</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miljenko_Jergovi%C4%87" title="Miljenko JergoviÄ">Miljenko JergoviÄ</a>, <a href="/wiki/Isak_Samokovlija" title="Isak Samokovlija">Isak Samokovlija</a>, <a href="/wiki/Safvet_beg_Ba%C5%A1agi%C4%87" class="mw-redirect" title="Safvet beg BaÅ¡agiÄ">Safvet beg BaÅ¡agiÄ</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abdulah_Sidran" title="Abdulah Sidran">Abdulah Sidran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Petar_Ko%C4%8Di%C4%87" title="Petar KoÄiÄ">Petar KoÄiÄ</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aleksandar_Hemon" title="Aleksandar Hemon">Aleksandar Hemon</a>, and NedÅ¾ad IbriÅ¡imoviÄ. The National Theater was founded 1919 in Sarajevo and its first director was the dramatist <a href="/wiki/Branislav_Nu%C5%A1i%C4%87" title="Branislav NuÅ¡iÄ">Branislav NuÅ¡iÄ</a>. Magazines such as <i><a href="/wiki/Novi_Plamen" title="Novi Plamen">Novi Plamen</a></i> or <i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://sveske.ba/en">Sarajevske sveske</a></i> are some of the more prominent publications covering cultural and literary themes. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art">Art</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Art_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" class="mw-redirect" title="Art of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Art of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bosniangraves_bosniska_gravar_februari_2007_stecak_stecci5.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Bosniangraves_bosniska_gravar_februari_2007_stecak_stecci5.jpg/230px-Bosniangraves_bosniska_gravar_februari_2007_stecak_stecci5.jpg" decoding="async" width="230" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Bosniangraves_bosniska_gravar_februari_2007_stecak_stecci5.jpg/345px-Bosniangraves_bosniska_gravar_februari_2007_stecak_stecci5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Bosniangraves_bosniska_gravar_februari_2007_stecak_stecci5.jpg/460px-Bosniangraves_bosniska_gravar_februari_2007_stecak_stecci5.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bosniangraves_bosniska_gravar_februari_2007_stecak_stecci5.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>SteÄci from Radimlja, near <a href="/wiki/Stolac" title="Stolac">Stolac</a> (13th century)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The art of Bosnia and Herzegovina was always evolving and ranged from the original medieval tombstones called <a href="/wiki/Ste%C4%87ci" class="mw-redirect" title="SteÄci">SteÄci</a> to paintings in <a href="/wiki/House_of_Kotromani%C4%87" class="mw-redirect" title="House of KotromaniÄ">KotromaniÄ</a> court. However, only with the arrival of Austro-Hungarians did the painting renaissance in Bosnia really begin to flourish. The first educated artists from European academies appeared with the beginning of the 20th century. Among those are: <a href="/wiki/Gabrijel_Jurki%C4%87" title="Gabrijel JurkiÄ">Gabrijel JurkiÄ</a>, <a href="/wiki/Petar_%C5%A0ain" title="Petar Å ain">Petar Å ain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roman_Petrovi%C4%87" title="Roman PetroviÄ">Roman PetroviÄ</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lazar_Drlja%C4%8Da" title="Lazar DrljaÄa">Lazar DrljaÄa</a>. </p>
      <p>After World War II artists like <a href="/wiki/Mersad_Berber" title="Mersad Berber">Mersad Berber</a> and <a href="/wiki/Safet_Zec" title="Safet Zec">Safet Zec</a> rose in popularity. </p>
      <p>In 2007, <a href="/wiki/Ars_Aevi" title="Ars Aevi">Ars Aevi</a>, a museum of contemporary art that includes works by renowned world artists was founded in Sarajevo. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:43._TKB_-_Seljo_z_Sarajewa_(Bo%C5%9Bnia_i_Hercegowina)_10.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/43._TKB_-_Seljo_z_Sarajewa_%28Bo%C5%9Bnia_i_Hercegowina%29_10.JPG/220px-43._TKB_-_Seljo_z_Sarajewa_%28Bo%C5%9Bnia_i_Hercegowina%29_10.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/43._TKB_-_Seljo_z_Sarajewa_%28Bo%C5%9Bnia_i_Hercegowina%29_10.JPG/330px-43._TKB_-_Seljo_z_Sarajewa_%28Bo%C5%9Bnia_i_Hercegowina%29_10.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/43._TKB_-_Seljo_z_Sarajewa_%28Bo%C5%9Bnia_i_Hercegowina%29_10.JPG/440px-43._TKB_-_Seljo_z_Sarajewa_%28Bo%C5%9Bnia_i_Hercegowina%29_10.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2576" data-file-height="1932"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:43._TKB_-_Seljo_z_Sarajewa_(Bo%C5%9Bnia_i_Hercegowina)_10.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Bosniaks dancing a traditional <a href="/wiki/Kolo_(dance)" title="Kolo (dance)">Kolo</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ensemble_%22Kolo%22,_%C4%90ur%C4%91evdan_customs_from_Podgrme%C4%8D.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Ensemble_%22Kolo%22%2C_%C4%90ur%C4%91evdan_customs_from_Podgrme%C4%8D.jpg/220px-Ensemble_%22Kolo%22%2C_%C4%90ur%C4%91evdan_customs_from_Podgrme%C4%8D.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Ensemble_%22Kolo%22%2C_%C4%90ur%C4%91evdan_customs_from_Podgrme%C4%8D.jpg/330px-Ensemble_%22Kolo%22%2C_%C4%90ur%C4%91evdan_customs_from_Podgrme%C4%8D.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Ensemble_%22Kolo%22%2C_%C4%90ur%C4%91evdan_customs_from_Podgrme%C4%8D.jpg/440px-Ensemble_%22Kolo%22%2C_%C4%90ur%C4%91evdan_customs_from_Podgrme%C4%8D.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3486" data-file-height="2615"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ensemble_%22Kolo%22,_%C4%90ur%C4%91evdan_customs_from_Podgrme%C4%8D.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Serbs from Bosanska Krajina in traditional clothing
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Music of Bosnia and Herzegovina">Music of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_patriotic_songs" title="List of Bosnia and Herzegovina patriotic songs">List of Bosnia and Herzegovina patriotic songs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_root_music" title="Bosnian root music">Bosnian root music</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Typical Bosnian and Herzegovinian songs are <i>ganga, rera</i>, and the traditional Slavic music for the folk dances such as <i><a href="/wiki/Kolo_(dance)" title="Kolo (dance)">kolo</a></i> and from Ottoman era the most popular is <a href="/wiki/Sevdalinka" title="Sevdalinka">sevdalinka</a>. Pop and Rock music has a tradition here as well, with the more famous musicians including <a href="/wiki/Dino_Zoni%C4%87" title="Dino ZoniÄ">Dino ZoniÄ</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goran_Bregovi%C4%87" title="Goran BregoviÄ">Goran BregoviÄ</a>, <a href="/wiki/Davorin_Popovi%C4%87" title="Davorin PopoviÄ">Davorin PopoviÄ</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kemal_Monteno" title="Kemal Monteno">Kemal Monteno</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zdravko_%C4%8Coli%C4%87" title="Zdravko ÄoliÄ">Zdravko ÄoliÄ</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elvir_Lakovi%C4%87" class="mw-redirect" title="Elvir LakoviÄ">Elvir LakoviÄ</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edo_Maajka" title="Edo Maajka">Edo Maajka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hari_Mata_Hari" title="Hari Mata Hari">Hari Mata Hari</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dino_Merlin" title="Dino Merlin">Dino Merlin</a>. Other composers such as <a href="/wiki/%C4%90or%C4%91e_Novkovi%C4%87" title="ÄorÄe NovkoviÄ">ÄorÄe NovkoviÄ</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al%27_Dino" title="Al' Dino">Al' Dino</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Haris_D%C5%BEinovi%C4%87&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Haris DÅ¾inoviÄ (page does not exist)">Haris DÅ¾inoviÄ</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kornelije_Kova%C4%8D" title="Kornelije KovaÄ">Kornelije KovaÄ</a>, and many pop and <a href="/wiki/Rock_bands" class="mw-redirect" title="Rock bands">rock bands</a>, for example, <a href="/wiki/Bijelo_dugme" class="mw-redirect" title="Bijelo dugme">Bijelo Dugme</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crvena_Jabuka" class="mw-redirect" title="Crvena Jabuka">Crvena Jabuka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Divlje_Jagode" class="mw-redirect" title="Divlje Jagode">Divlje Jagode</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indexi" title="Indexi">Indexi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plavi_orkestar" title="Plavi orkestar">Plavi Orkestar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zabranjeno_Pu%C5%A1enje" title="Zabranjeno PuÅ¡enje">Zabranjeno PuÅ¡enje</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ambasadori" title="Ambasadori">Ambasadori</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dubioza_kolektiv" title="Dubioza kolektiv">Dubioza kolektiv</a>, who were among the leading ones in the former Yugoslavia. Bosnia is home to the composer <a href="/wiki/Du%C5%A1an_%C5%A0esti%C4%87" title="DuÅ¡an Å estiÄ">DuÅ¡an Å estiÄ</a>, the creator of the <a href="/wiki/National_anthem" title="National anthem">national anthem</a> of Bosnia and Herzegovina and father of singer <a href="/wiki/Marija_%C5%A0esti%C4%87" title="Marija Å estiÄ">Marija Å estiÄ</a>, to the world known jazz musician, educator and Bosnian jazz ambassador <a href="/wiki/Sinan_Alimanovi%C4%87" title="Sinan AlimanoviÄ">Sinan AlimanoviÄ</a>, composer <a href="/wiki/Sa%C5%A1a_Lo%C5%A1i%C4%87" title="SaÅ¡a LoÅ¡iÄ">SaÅ¡a LoÅ¡iÄ</a> and pianist <a href="/wiki/Sa%C5%A1a_Toperi%C4%87" title="SaÅ¡a ToperiÄ">SaÅ¡a ToperiÄ</a>. In the villages, especially in Herzegovina, Bosniaks, Serbs, and Croats play the ancient <i><a href="/wiki/Gusle" title="Gusle">Gusle</a></i>. The gusle is used mainly to recite epic poems in a usually dramatic tone. </p>
      <p>Probably the most distinctive and identifiably "Bosnian" of music, Sevdalinka is a kind of emotional, melancholic folk song that often describes sad subjects such as love and loss, the death of a dear person or heartbreak. Sevdalinkas were traditionally performed with a <a href="/wiki/Saz_(musical_instrument)" class="mw-redirect" title="Saz (musical instrument)">saz</a>, a Turkish string instrument, which was later replaced by the accordion. However the more modern arrangement, to the derision of some purists, is typically a vocalist accompanied by the accordion along with snare drums, upright bass, guitars, clarinets and violins. </p>
      <p>Rural folk traditions in Bosnia and Herzegovina include the shouted, <a href="/wiki/Polyphony" title="Polyphony">polyphonic</a> <a href="/wiki/Ganga_(music)" title="Ganga (music)">ganga</a> and "ravne pjesme" (<i>flat song</i>) styles, as well as instruments like a droneless <a href="/wiki/Bagpipe" class="mw-redirect" title="Bagpipe">bagpipe</a>, wooden <a href="/wiki/Flute" title="Flute">flute</a> and <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0argija" title="Å argija">Å¡argija</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Gusle" title="Gusle">gusle</a>, an instrument found throughout the <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a>, is also used to accompany ancient <a href="/wiki/Slavic_peoples" class="mw-redirect" title="Slavic peoples">Slavic</a> <a href="/wiki/Epic_poetry" title="Epic poetry">epic</a> <a href="/wiki/Poems" class="mw-redirect" title="Poems">poems</a>. There are also Bosnian folk songs in the <a href="/wiki/Judeo-Spanish" class="mw-redirect" title="Judeo-Spanish">Ladino</a> language, derived from the area's Jewish population. </p>
      <p><i>Bosnian roots music</i> came from <a href="/wiki/Central_Bosnia_Canton" title="Central Bosnia Canton">Middle Bosnia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Posavina" title="Posavina">Posavina</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Drina" title="Drina">Drina</a> valley and <a href="/wiki/Kalesija" title="Kalesija">Kalesija</a>. It is usually performed by singers with two violinists and a <a href="/wiki/Sargija" class="mw-redirect" title="Sargija">Å¡argija</a> player. These bands first appeared around <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> and became popular in the 1960s. This is the third oldest music following after the <a href="/wiki/Sevdalinka" title="Sevdalinka">sevdalinka</a> and ilahija. Self-taught people, mostly in two or three members of the different choices of old instruments, mostly in the violin, sacking, <a href="/wiki/Ba%C4%9Flama" title="BaÄlama">saz</a>, drums, flutes (zurle) or wooden flute, as others have already called, the original performers of Bosnian music that can not be written notes, transmitted by ear from generation to generation, family is usually hereditary. It is thought to be brought from Persia-Kalesi tribe that settled in the area of present Sprecanski valleys and hence probably the name Kalesija. In this part of Bosnia it is the most common. Again, it became the leader of First World War onwards, as well as 60 years in the field Sprecanski doline. This kind of music was enjoyed by all three peoples in Bosnia, Bosniaks, Croats and Serbs, and it contributed a lot to reconcile people socializing, entertainment and other organizations through festivala. In Kalesija it is maintained each year with the Bosnian Festival Original music. </p>
      <p>Studio Kemix firm Dzemal Dzihanovic from <a href="/wiki/%C5%BDivinice" title="Å½ivinice">Å½ivinice</a> together with his artists brought this kind of music to perfection at the end 20th century. With its entirely new form of modernity, it is most common in the <a href="/wiki/Tuzla_Canton" title="Tuzla Canton">Tuzla Canton</a> and the cradle of this music city <a href="/wiki/%C5%BDivinice" title="Å½ivinice">Å½ivinice</a> was named Bosnian town of original music. Songs are performed preferably in a <a href="/wiki/Diphthong" title="Diphthong">diphthong</a>, the first and second voice which is a special secret performance of this music and some performers sing in troglasju as they do Kalesijski triple that was recorded in 1968, as the first written record of the tone on the album, along with Higurashi no naku. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinema_and_theatre">Cinema and theatre</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Bosnia-Herzegovina_films" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Bosnia-Herzegovina films">List of Bosnia-Herzegovina films</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Sarajevo is internationally renowned for its eclectic and diverse selection of festivals. The <a href="/wiki/Sarajevo_Film_Festival" title="Sarajevo Film Festival">Sarajevo Film Festival</a> was established in 1995, during the Bosnian War and has become the premier and largest film festival in the Balkans and South-East Europe. </p>
      <p>Bosnia has a rich cinematic and film heritage, dating back to the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Yugoslavia" title="Kingdom of Yugoslavia">Kingdom of Yugoslavia</a>; many Bosnian filmmakers have achieved international prominence and some have won international awards ranging from the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Academy Awards</a> to multiple <a href="/wiki/Palme_d%27Or" title="Palme d'Or">Palme d'Ors</a> and <a href="/wiki/Golden_Bear" title="Golden Bear">Golden Bears</a>. Some notable Bosnian screenwriters, directors and producers are <a href="/wiki/Danis_Tanovi%C4%87" title="Danis TanoviÄ">Danis TanoviÄ</a> (known for the Academy Awardâ and <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden Globe Award">Golden Globe Award</a>âwinning 2001 film <i><a href="/wiki/No_Man%27s_Land_(2001_film)" title="No Man's Land (2001 film)">No Man's Land</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Jury_Grand_Prix" class="mw-redirect" title="Jury Grand Prix">Silver Bear Grand Jury Prize</a>âwinning 2016 film <i><a href="/wiki/Death_in_Sarajevo" title="Death in Sarajevo">Death in Sarajevo</a></i>),<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[191]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Emir_Kusturica" title="Emir Kusturica">Emir Kusturica</a> (won two <a href="/wiki/Palme_d%27Or" title="Palme d'Or">Palme d'Or</a> at Cannes), <a href="/wiki/Jasmila_%C5%BDbani%C4%87" title="Jasmila Å½baniÄ">Jasmila Å½baniÄ</a> (won Golden Bear), <a href="/wiki/Zlatko_Top%C4%8Di%C4%87" title="Zlatko TopÄiÄ">Zlatko TopÄiÄ</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ademir_Kenovi%C4%87" title="Ademir KenoviÄ">Ademir KenoviÄ</a>, Dino MustafiÄ, <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_Imamovi%C4%87" title="Ahmed ImamoviÄ">Ahmed ImamoviÄ</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pjer_%C5%BDalica" title="Pjer Å½alica">Pjer Å½alica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aida_Begi%C4%87" title="Aida BegiÄ">Aida BegiÄ</a>, Adis BakraÄ, etc. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_cuisine" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina cuisine">Bosnia and Herzegovina cuisine</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bosnian_meat_platter.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Bosnian_meat_platter.JPG/240px-Bosnian_meat_platter.JPG" decoding="async" width="240" height="180" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Bosnian_meat_platter.JPG/360px-Bosnian_meat_platter.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Bosnian_meat_platter.JPG/480px-Bosnian_meat_platter.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2592"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bosnian_meat_platter.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Bosnian meat platter
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Bosnian cuisine uses many spices, in moderate quantities. Most dishes are light, as they are boiled; the sauces are fully natural, consisting of little more than the natural juices of the vegetables in the dish. Typical ingredients include tomatoes, potatoes, onions, <a href="/wiki/Garlic" title="Garlic">garlic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Capsicum" title="Capsicum">peppers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cucumber" title="Cucumber">cucumbers</a>, carrots, <a href="/wiki/Cabbage" title="Cabbage">cabbage</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mushroom" title="Mushroom">mushrooms</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spinach" title="Spinach">spinach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zucchini" title="Zucchini">zucchini</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bean" title="Bean">dried beans</a>, fresh beans, <a href="/wiki/Plum" title="Plum">plums</a>, milk, <a href="/wiki/Paprika" title="Paprika">paprika</a> and cream called <a href="/wiki/Smetana_(dairy_product)" title="Smetana (dairy product)">Pavlaka</a>. Bosnian cuisine is balanced between <a href="/wiki/Western_culture" title="Western culture">Western</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_world" title="Eastern world">Eastern</a> influences. As a result of the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_cuisine" title="Turkish cuisine">Ottoman</a> administration for almost 500 years, Bosnian food is closely related to <a href="/wiki/Turkish_cuisine" title="Turkish cuisine">Turkish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greek_cuisine" title="Greek cuisine">Greek</a>, and other former <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_cuisine" title="Mediterranean cuisine">Mediterranean</a> cuisines. However, because of years of Austrian rule, there are many influences from Central Europe. Typical meat dishes include primarily beef and <a href="/wiki/Lamb_and_mutton" title="Lamb and mutton">lamb</a>. Some local specialties are <a href="/wiki/%C4%86evap%C4%8Di%C4%87i" class="mw-redirect" title="ÄevapÄiÄi">Äevapi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burek" class="mw-redirect" title="Burek">burek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dolma" title="Dolma">dolma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sarma_(food)" title="Sarma (food)">sarma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pilav" class="mw-redirect" title="Pilav">pilav</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goulash" title="Goulash">goulash</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ajvar" title="Ajvar">ajvar</a> and a whole range of Eastern sweets. Äevapi is a grilled dish of minced meat, a type of <a href="/wiki/Kebab" title="Kebab">kebab</a>, popular in former Yugoslavia and considered a national dish in Bosnia and Herzegovina<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[192]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[193]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[194]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[195]</a></sup> Local wines come from <a href="/wiki/Herzegovina" title="Herzegovina">Herzegovina</a> where the climate is suitable for growing grapes. Herzegovinian <i>loza</i> (similar to Italian <a href="/wiki/Grappa" title="Grappa">Grappa</a> but less sweet) is very popular. Plum (<i>rakija</i>) or apple (<i>jabukovaÄa</i>) alcohol beverages are produced in the north. In the south, distilleries used to produce vast quantities of <a href="/wiki/Brandy" title="Brandy">brandy</a> and supply all of ex-Yugoslav alcohol factories (brandy is the base of most <a href="/wiki/Alcoholic_beverage" class="mw-redirect" title="Alcoholic beverage">alcoholic drinks</a>). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Leisure_activities">Leisure activities</span></h3> 
      <p>Coffeehouses, where <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_coffee" class="mw-redirect" title="Bosnian coffee">Bosnian coffee</a> is served in <a href="/wiki/Cezve" title="Cezve">dÅ¾ezva</a> with <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Delight" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkish Delight">rahat lokum</a> and sugar cubes, proliferate <a href="/wiki/Sarajevo" title="Sarajevo">Sarajevo</a> and every city in the country. Coffee drinking is a favorite Bosnian pastime and part of the culture. Bosnia and Herzegovina is the ninth country in the entire world by per capita coffee consumption.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[196]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_at_the_Olympics" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina at the Olympics">Bosnia and Herzegovina at the Olympics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Football_in_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Football in Bosnia and Herzegovina">Football in Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Asim_Ferhatovi%C4%87_Hase_Stadium.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Asim_Ferhatovi%C4%87_Hase_Stadium.jpg/220px-Asim_Ferhatovi%C4%87_Hase_Stadium.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Asim_Ferhatovi%C4%87_Hase_Stadium.jpg/330px-Asim_Ferhatovi%C4%87_Hase_Stadium.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Asim_Ferhatovi%C4%87_Hase_Stadium.jpg/440px-Asim_Ferhatovi%C4%87_Hase_Stadium.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="853"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Asim_Ferhatovi%C4%87_Hase_Stadium.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Asim_Ferhatovi%C4%87_Hase_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Asim FerhatoviÄ Hase Stadium">Asim FerhatoviÄ Hase Stadium</a> in Sarajevo hosted the opening ceremony to the <a href="/wiki/1984_Winter_Olympics" title="1984 Winter Olympics">1984 Winter Olympics</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:20150331_2026_AUT_BIH_2177_Edin_D%C5%BEeko.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/20150331_2026_AUT_BIH_2177_Edin_D%C5%BEeko.jpg/180px-20150331_2026_AUT_BIH_2177_Edin_D%C5%BEeko.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="271" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/20150331_2026_AUT_BIH_2177_Edin_D%C5%BEeko.jpg/270px-20150331_2026_AUT_BIH_2177_Edin_D%C5%BEeko.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/20150331_2026_AUT_BIH_2177_Edin_D%C5%BEeko.jpg/360px-20150331_2026_AUT_BIH_2177_Edin_D%C5%BEeko.jpg 2x" data-file-width="660" data-file-height="992"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:20150331_2026_AUT_BIH_2177_Edin_D%C5%BEeko.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>

        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Bosnia and Herzegovina has produced many athletes, both as a state in Yugoslavia and independently after 1992. The most important international <a href="/wiki/Sport" title="Sport">sporting event</a> in the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="History of Bosnia and Herzegovina">history of Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> was the <a href="/wiki/1984_Winter_Olympics" title="1984 Winter Olympics">14th Winter Olympics</a>, held in <a href="/wiki/Sarajevo" title="Sarajevo">Sarajevo</a> from 7 to 19 February 1984. The <a href="/wiki/RK_Borac_Banja_Luka" title="RK Borac Banja Luka">Borac</a> <a href="/wiki/Team_handball" class="mw-redirect" title="Team handball">handball</a> club has won seven <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_Handball_Championship" title="Yugoslav Handball Championship">Yugoslav Handball Championships</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/EHF_Champions_League" title="EHF Champions League">European Championship Cup</a> in <a href="/wiki/1975%E2%80%9376_European_Cup_(handball)" title="1975â76 European Cup (handball)">1976</a> and the <a href="/wiki/EHF_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="EHF Cup">International Handball Federation Cup</a> in 1991. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Amel_Meki%C4%87" title="Amel MekiÄ">Amel MekiÄ</a>, Bosnian judoka, became <a href="/wiki/2011_European_Judo_Championships" title="2011 European Judo Championships">European champion</a> in 2011. Track and field athlete <a href="/wiki/Amel_Tuka" title="Amel Tuka">Amel Tuka</a> won bronze and silver medals in 800 metres at the <a href="/wiki/2015_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="2015 World Championships in Athletics">2015</a> and <a href="/wiki/2019_World_Athletics_Championships" title="2019 World Athletics Championships">2019 World Athletics Championships</a><sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[197]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Hamza_Ali%C4%87" title="Hamza AliÄ">Hamza AliÄ</a> won the silver medal in <a href="/wiki/2013_European_Athletics_Indoor_Championships_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_shot_put" title="2013 European Athletics Indoor Championships â Men's shot put">shot put</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2013_European_Athletics_Indoor_Championships" title="2013 European Athletics Indoor Championships">2013 European Indoor Championships</a>. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/KK_Bosna" class="mw-redirect" title="KK Bosna">Bosna Royal</a> basketball club from Sarajevo were <a href="/wiki/Euroleague_Basketball" title="Euroleague Basketball">European Champions</a> in <a href="/wiki/1978%E2%80%9379_FIBA_European_Champions_Cup" title="1978â79 FIBA European Champions Cup">1979</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia_national_basketball_team" title="Yugoslavia national basketball team">Yugoslav national basketball team</a>, which won medals in every world championship from 1963 through 1990, included Bosnian players such as <a href="/wiki/FIBA_Hall_of_Fame" title="FIBA Hall of Fame">FIBA Hall of Famers</a> <a href="/wiki/Dra%C5%BEen_Dalipagi%C4%87" title="DraÅ¾en DalipagiÄ">DraÅ¾en DalipagiÄ</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mirza_Deliba%C5%A1i%C4%87" title="Mirza DelibaÅ¡iÄ">Mirza DelibaÅ¡iÄ</a>. Bosnia and Herzegovina regularly qualifies for the <a href="/wiki/EuroBasket" title="EuroBasket">European Championship in Basketball</a>, with players including <a href="/wiki/Mirza_Teletovi%C4%87" title="Mirza TeletoviÄ">Mirza TeletoviÄ</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nihad_%C4%90edovi%C4%87" title="Nihad ÄedoviÄ">Nihad ÄedoviÄ</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jusuf_Nurki%C4%87" title="Jusuf NurkiÄ">Jusuf NurkiÄ</a>. <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_men%27s_national_under-16_and_under-17_basketball_team" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina men's national under-16 and under-17 basketball team">Bosnia and Herzegovina national u-16 team</a> won two gold medals in 2015, winning both <a href="/wiki/Basketball_at_the_2015_European_Youth_Summer_Olympic_Festival" title="Basketball at the 2015 European Youth Summer Olympic Festival">2015 European Youth Summer Olympic Festival</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/2015_FIBA_Europe_Under-16_Championship" title="2015 FIBA Europe Under-16 Championship">2015 FIBA Europe Under-16 Championship</a>. </p>
      <p>Women's basketball club <a href="/wiki/%C5%BDKK_Jedinstvo_Tuzla" title="Å½KK Jedinstvo Tuzla">Jedinstvo Aida</a> from Tuzla won <a href="/wiki/EuroLeague_Women" title="EuroLeague Women">Women's European Club Championship</a> in 1989 and <a href="/wiki/Ronchetti_Cup" title="Ronchetti Cup">Ronchetti Cup</a> final in 1990, led by <a href="/wiki/Razija_Mujanovi%C4%87" title="Razija MujanoviÄ">Razija MujanoviÄ</a>, three times best female European basketball player, and <a href="/wiki/Mara_Laki%C4%87" title="Mara LakiÄ">Mara LakiÄ</a> </p>
      <p>The Bosnian <a href="/wiki/Chess" title="Chess">chess</a> team was <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_Chess_Championship" title="Yugoslav Chess Championship">Champion of Yugoslavia</a> seven times, in addition to club <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0K_Bosna" title="Å K Bosna">Å K Bosna</a> winning four <a href="/wiki/European_Chess_Club_Cup" title="European Chess Club Cup">European Chess Club Cups</a>. Chess grandmaster <a href="/wiki/Borki_Predojevi%C4%87" title="Borki PredojeviÄ">Borki PredojeviÄ</a> has also won two European Championships. The most impressive success of Bosnian Chess was runner-up position in <a href="/wiki/31st_Chess_Olympiad" title="31st Chess Olympiad">Chess Olympiad</a> of 1994 in <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a>, featuring Grandmasters <a href="/wiki/Predrag_Nikoli%C4%87" title="Predrag NikoliÄ">Predrag NikoliÄ</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Sokolov_(chess_player)" title="Ivan Sokolov (chess player)">Ivan Sokolov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bojan_Kurajica" title="Bojan Kurajica">Bojan Kurajica</a>. </p>
      <p>Middle-weight <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxer</a> <a href="/wiki/Marijan_Bene%C5%A1" title="Marijan BeneÅ¡">Marijan BeneÅ¡</a> has won several Championships of Bosnia and Herzegovina, Yugoslav Championships and the <a href="/wiki/European_Amateur_Boxing_Championships" title="European Amateur Boxing Championships">European Championship</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nezavisne_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nezavisne-200">[198]</a></sup> In 1978, he won the World Title against <a href="/wiki/Elisha_Obed" title="Elisha Obed">Elisha Obed</a> from the Bahamas. </p>
      <p>Association football is the most popular sport in Bosnia and Herzegovina. It dates from 1903, but its popularity grew significantly after World War I. Bosnian clubs <a href="/wiki/FK_Sarajevo" title="FK Sarajevo">FK Sarajevo</a> and <a href="/wiki/FK_%C5%BDeljezni%C4%8Dar_Sarajevo" title="FK Å½eljezniÄar Sarajevo">Å½eljezniÄar</a>, won the <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_First_League" title="Yugoslav First League">Yugoslav Championship</a>, while the <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia_national_football_team" title="Yugoslavia national football team">Yugoslav national football team</a> included Bosnian players of all ethnic backgrounds and generations, such as <a href="/wiki/Safet_Su%C5%A1i%C4%87" title="Safet SuÅ¡iÄ">Safet SuÅ¡iÄ</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zlatko_Vujovi%C4%87" title="Zlatko VujoviÄ">Zlatko VujoviÄ</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mehmed_Ba%C5%BEdarevi%C4%87" title="Mehmed BaÅ¾dareviÄ">Mehmed BaÅ¾dareviÄ</a>, <a href="/wiki/Davor_Jozi%C4%87" title="Davor JoziÄ">Davor JoziÄ</a>, <a href="/wiki/Faruk_Had%C5%BEibegi%C4%87" title="Faruk HadÅ¾ibegiÄ">Faruk HadÅ¾ibegiÄ</a>, <a href="/wiki/Predrag_Pa%C5%A1i%C4%87" title="Predrag PaÅ¡iÄ">Predrag PaÅ¡iÄ</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bla%C5%BE_Sli%C5%A1kovi%C4%87" title="BlaÅ¾ SliÅ¡koviÄ">BlaÅ¾ SliÅ¡koviÄ</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vahid_Halilhod%C5%BEi%C4%87" title="Vahid HalilhodÅ¾iÄ">Vahid HalilhodÅ¾iÄ</a>, <a href="/wiki/Du%C5%A1an_Bajevi%C4%87" title="DuÅ¡an BajeviÄ">DuÅ¡an BajeviÄ</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ivica_Osim" title="Ivica Osim">Ivica Osim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Josip_Katalinski" title="Josip Katalinski">Josip Katalinski</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tomislav_Knez" title="Tomislav Knez">Tomislav Knez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Velimir_Sombolac" title="Velimir Sombolac">Velimir Sombolac</a> and numerous others. The <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_national_football_team" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina national football team">Bosnia and Herzegovina national football team</a> played at the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014 FIFA World Cup</a>, its first major tournament. Players on the team again includes notable players of all country's ethnic background, such as then and now captains <a href="/wiki/Emir_Spahi%C4%87" title="Emir SpahiÄ">Emir SpahiÄ</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zvjezdan_Misimovi%C4%87" title="Zvjezdan MisimoviÄ">Zvjezdan MisimoviÄ</a> and <a href="/wiki/Edin_D%C5%BEeko" title="Edin DÅ¾eko">Edin DÅ¾eko</a>, defenders like <a href="/wiki/Ognjen_Vranje%C5%A1" title="Ognjen VranjeÅ¡">Ognjen VranjeÅ¡</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sead_Kola%C5%A1inac" title="Sead KolaÅ¡inac">Sead KolaÅ¡inac</a> and <a href="/wiki/Toni_%C5%A0unji%C4%87" title="Toni Å unjiÄ">Toni Å unjiÄ</a>, midfielders like <a href="/wiki/Miralem_Pjani%C4%87" title="Miralem PjaniÄ">Miralem PjaniÄ</a> and <a href="/wiki/Senad_Luli%C4%87" title="Senad LuliÄ">Senad LuliÄ</a>, striker <a href="/wiki/Vedad_Ibi%C5%A1evi%C4%87" title="Vedad IbiÅ¡eviÄ">Vedad IbiÅ¡eviÄ</a>, and so on. </p>
      <p>Former Bosnian footballers include <a href="/wiki/Hasan_Salihamid%C5%BEi%C4%87" title="Hasan SalihamidÅ¾iÄ">Hasan SalihamidÅ¾iÄ</a>, who became only the second Bosnian to ever win a <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> trophy, after <a href="/wiki/Elvir_Balji%C4%87" title="Elvir BaljiÄ">Elvir BaljiÄ</a>. He made 234 appearances and scored 31 goals for German club <a href="/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich" title="FC Bayern Munich">FC Bayern Munich</a>. <a href="/wiki/Sergej_Barbarez" title="Sergej Barbarez">Sergej Barbarez</a>, who played for several clubs in the German <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga" title="Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a> including <a href="/wiki/Borussia_Dortmund" title="Borussia Dortmund">Borussia Dortmund</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hamburger_SV" title="Hamburger SV">Hamburger SV</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bayer_Leverkusen" class="mw-redirect" title="Bayer Leverkusen">Bayer Leverkusen</a> was joint-top scorer in the <a href="/wiki/2000%E2%80%9301_Bundesliga" title="2000â01 Bundesliga">2000â01 Bundesliga</a> season with 22 goals. <a href="/wiki/Meho_Kodro" title="Meho Kodro">Meho Kodro</a> spent most of his career playing in <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> most notably with <a href="/wiki/Real_Sociedad" title="Real Sociedad">Real Sociedad</a> and <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">FC Barcelona</a>. <a href="/wiki/Elvir_Rahimi%C4%87" title="Elvir RahimiÄ">Elvir RahimiÄ</a> made 302 appearances for Russian club <a href="/wiki/CSKA_Moscow" title="CSKA Moscow">CSKA Moscow</a> with whom he won the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="UEFA Cup">UEFA Cup</a> in <a href="/wiki/2005_UEFA_Cup_Final" title="2005 UEFA Cup Final">2005</a>. <a href="/wiki/Milena_Nikoli%C4%87" title="Milena NikoliÄ">Milena NikoliÄ</a>, member of <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_women%27s_national_football_team" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina women's national football team">women's national team</a>, was <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_UEFA_Women%27s_Champions_League" title="2013â14 UEFA Women's Champions League">2013â14 UEFA Women's Champions League</a> <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Women%27s_Champions_League#Top_scorers" title="UEFA Women's Champions League">top scorer</a>. </p>
      <p>Bosnia and Herzegovina was the world champion of <a href="/wiki/Volleyball_at_the_2004_Summer_Paralympics" title="Volleyball at the 2004 Summer Paralympics">volleyball at the 2004 Summer Paralympics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Volleyball_at_the_2012_Summer_Paralympics" title="Volleyball at the 2012 Summer Paralympics">volleyball at the 2012 Summer Paralympics</a>. Many among those on the team lost their legs in the Bosnian War. Its <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_national_sitting_volleyball_team" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina national sitting volleyball team">national sitting volleyball team</a> is one of the dominant forces in <a href="/wiki/Sitting_volleyball" title="Sitting volleyball">the sport</a> worldwide, winning nine European Championships, three World Championships and two <a href="/wiki/Volleyball_at_the_Summer_Paralympics" title="Volleyball at the Summer Paralympics">Paralympic</a> gold medals. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">Tennis</a> is also gaining a lot of popularity after the recent successes of <a href="/wiki/Damir_D%C5%BEumhur" title="Damir DÅ¾umhur">Damir DÅ¾umhur</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mirza_Ba%C5%A1i%C4%87" title="Mirza BaÅ¡iÄ">Mirza BaÅ¡iÄ</a> at <a href="/wiki/Grand_Slam_(tennis)" title="Grand Slam (tennis)">Grand Slam</a> level. Other notable tennis players who represented Bosnia are, <a href="/wiki/Amer_Deli%C4%87" title="Amer DeliÄ">Amer DeliÄ</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mervana_Jugi%C4%87-Salki%C4%87" title="Mervana JugiÄ-SalkiÄ">Mervana JugiÄ-SalkiÄ</a>. </p>

         <td align="right" valign="top">a.&nbsp;&nbsp; </td> 
         <td><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_status"><b><a href="#ref_status">^</a></b></span> Kosovo is the subject of a territorial dispute between the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Republic of Kosovo</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Republic of Serbia</a>. The Republic of Kosovo <a href="/wiki/2008_Kosovo_declaration_of_independence" title="2008 Kosovo declaration of independence">unilaterally declared independence</a> on 17 February 2008. <a href="/wiki/Kosovo%E2%80%93Serbia_relations" title="KosovoâSerbia relations">Serbia continues to claim</a> it as part of its <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Province_of_Kosovo_and_Metohija" title="Autonomous Province of Kosovo and Metohija">own sovereign territory</a>. The two governments <a href="/wiki/Belgrade%E2%80%93Pristina_negotiations" title="BelgradeâPristina negotiations">began to normalise relations</a> in 2013, as part of the <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Agreement_(2013)" title="Brussels Agreement (2013)">2013 Brussels Agreement</a>. Kosovo is currently recognized as an independent state by <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Kosovo" title="International recognition of Kosovo">98</a> out of the 193 <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_United_Nations" title="Member states of the United Nations">United Nations member states</a>. In total, <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Kosovo" title="International recognition of Kosovo">113</a> UN member states recognized Kosovo at some point, of which <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Kosovo" title="International recognition of Kosovo">15</a> later withdrew their recognition. </td>
        </tr>
